Insider)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f7cb23394fce90018f7b6de?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn75@2020_2/2020/10/19/15-59-49-142_55aec9418fd41619.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn56@2020_5/2020/10/19/15-59-47-418_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=Fb8n4gmr9Rw:DfWdoTN8xXY:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn44@2020_4/2020/10/19/15-59-42-762_bf0421bee0f40a32.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=Fb8n4gmr9Rw:DfWdoTN8xXY:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn71@2020_1/2020/10/19/15-59-45-249_d0ace092225a7c63.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn91@2020_5/2020/10/19/15-59-43-999_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=Fb8n4gmr9Rw:DfWdoTN8xXY:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn79@2020_4/2020/10/19/15-59-43-062_0d5e87789aa41013.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/Fb8n4gmr9Rw":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn52@2020_3/2020/10/19/15-59-38-905_e8118b3750145441.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1603123146001},{"createdTime":"2020-10-19 23:59:05","updatedTime":"2020-10-19 23:59:05","title":"The 4 main types of procrastinators and how to not be one of them, according to 2 accountability coaches","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/main-types-of-procrastinators-how-to-avoid-accountability-coaches","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5db8706fdee01906084e71b7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Ali Schiller and Marissa Boisvert\" height=\"3147\" width=\"4196\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Ali Schiller and Marissa Boisvert.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Courtesy of Ali Schiller and Marissa Boisvert</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Ali Schiller and Marissa Boisvert are the co-owners of <a href=\"https://accountabilityworks.com/\">Accountability Works</a>, where they coach professionals on accomplishing their goals without sacrificing their health.</li>\n<li>They say that there are four main types of avoidance archetypes, or procrastinators: the performer, the self-deprecator, the overbooker, and the novelty seeker.</li>\n<li>Figuring out which group you're in can help you break out of your procrastination patterns &#8212; and maybe even turn in something early.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>As accountability coaches, we work with highly-driven, accomplished entrepreneurs.</p><p>Just in case you have any doubt, highly-driven, accomplished people procrastinate, too. We've heard every excuse under the sun. Procrastination is a habit, and if you understand how it shows up for you, you can replace it with a better one.</p><p>Here are two clients' examples:</p><p>Brian called in to his weekly accountability call one morning exhausted and disappointed. He had gotten everything he committed to done. But he'd stayed up all night to do it. Although this habit worked well when he was single and doing contract work on his own schedule, now as a successful consultant, husband, and father, he was ready to make a change.&#160;</p><p>Our client Melinda is at the top of her game: accomplished, polished, and the CEO of a successful marketing company. While she would never claim the title of procrastinator, she had shiny object syndrome and couldn't finish a project without starting a new one.</p><p>How can highly-driven and accomplished people <em>still</em> be such procrastinators?&#160;</p><p>Let's be real: We can all fall into this trap. As accountability coaches we've learned that what works for Brian doesn't necessarily work for Melinda.&#160;</p><p>In our experience, everyone has a favorite avoidance archetype. The key to defeating delay is figuring out which group you fall into so you can break out of your holding pattern and get the project done <em>early</em>, for once.&#160;</p><p>Here's a breakdown of the procrastination personality types and how to retrain your brain to finally get <em>any </em>dreaded task done.</p><h2><strong>1. The performer who says, \"I work well under pressure\"</strong></h2><p>This procrastinator forces themselves to focus by shrinking the time they have to tackle a task. For many of our clients, the real reason behind this is perfectionism. If you're tight on time, there's no way the task can be done to your unreasonably high standards anyway, right? For others, the issue is simply falling back into old patterns and beliefs that we have about our 11th-hour saves. No matter what, being in the habit of putting pressure on yourself is not sustainable.</p><p><strong>Your biggest challenge:</strong> Getting started.</p><p><strong>Your solution</strong>: Flip the script and set a start date. When you focus on when you're going to begin a task — and not when you hope to end it — you'll take a tremendous amount of pressure off of yourself.</p><h2><strong>2. The self-deprecator who says, \"I am so lazy right now\"</strong><strong><br></strong></h2><p>This procrastinator is the opposite of lazy, so when they don't do something they are extra hard on themselves. We see this a lot with our male clients. They tend to blame inaction on laziness or stubbornness rather than admit they are tired. What they <em>really</em> need is to be more compassionate with themselves.&#160;</p><p><strong>Your biggest challenge:</strong> Taking a break. We already know you are going to say you don't have time to rest.&#160;</p><p><strong>Your solution:</strong> Recharge. Try taking a walk to give yourself space and to begin to rebuild your energy.&#160;</p><h2><strong>3. The overbooker who says, \"I'm so busy\"</strong></h2><p>This procrastinator is a pro at filling up their calendar and is often overwhelmed. \"I'm so busy\" is probably the excuse we hear most often. Interestingly, some of the busiest people we work with get the most done. When busy-ness comes up as an excuse for not doing something, it's usually an indication of avoidance. Rather than facing a challenge head on or admitting they don't want to do something, it's easier to place the blame on having other important things to do.&#160;</p><p><strong>Your biggest challenge:</strong> Creating chaos to avoid facing what you know you need to face right now (typically this is not a task).</p><p><strong>Your solution:</strong> Take a moment of introspection. Ask yourself: W<em>hat am I really avoiding?</em></p><h2><strong>4. The novelty seeker who says, \"I just had the best idea!\"</strong></h2><p>This procrastinator has a terminal case of Shiny Object Syndrome. They're constantly coming up with new projects to take on — and then getting bored with them a week later. They're intrigued by the latest trend and will be quick to implement but not follow through.&#160;</p><p>They are great at making decisions and taking action. However, they end up inadvertently losing a lot of time and burning out because they don't take consistent action in one direction long enough to see results. Many of our entrepreneurial clients fit into this category.&#160;</p><p><strong>Your biggest challenge:</strong> Completion.</p><p><strong>Your solution:</strong> Make it stick. Literally. Write down new ideas or projects on a sticky note — but don't pursue them until you finish what you are currently working on.&#160;</p><p><em>Ali Schiller and Marissa Boisvert are the co-owners of Accountability Works®, a mindfulness-based coaching company that helps highly-driven professionals accomplish their goals without sacrificing their health. Using their five-step process, they have provided the structure their clients need to do everything from tripling their income, getting into a top tier MBA program, losing 100 lbs — and so much more. You can download their </em><a href=\"https://accountabilityworks.com/map_it\"><em>Map It! 1-Page Plan</em></a><em> to help you organize and achieve your goals.</em></p><p><em>This Business Insider article was originally published on October 30, 2019.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a The North America box office stands at $1.94 billion as the US theatrical market continues to struggle amid the coronavirus pandemic.&#160;</p><p>The China market has been <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/china-box-office-rebounding-as-us-theaters-struggle-2020-10\">boosted by local blockbusters</a> like \"My People, My Homeland\" and the animated \"Legend of Deification,\" which both earned more than $150 million in one weekend earlier this month during China's National Day and Mid-Autumn Festival holiday period.</p><p>US releases in China haven't fared as well. Disney's live-action \"Mulan\" remake was supposed to be a major hit in China, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mulan-flops-at-china-box-office-in-its-debut-weekend-2020-9\">but has flopped</a> with just $40 million since opening in September. Warner Bros. \"Tenet\" has earned $64 million in the region (but $334 million globally).</p><p>This past weekend's China box office was down 32% from the same period last year, but the recovery is impressive considering all 70,000 of the region's movie theaters were shut down for six months this year.</p><p>US theaters were closed from March to August, but its post-reopening box office has come nowhere near the kind of numbers China is experiencing right now.</p><p>The major chains Regal and Cineworld recently closed all theaters in the US and US again. src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f077b2ff34d0566dd5ba1c8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"business owner ecommerce resale entrepreneur\" height=\"2000\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Optimize your ecommerce business with a great user experience and diversified channels.\n<p class=\"copyright\">eclipse_images/Getty</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Many brick-and-mortar stores are transitioning to ecommerce to attract new customers during the coronavirus pandemic.&#160;</li>\n<li>From clicking on the landing page to making a final purchase, every step of the online user experience is critical to converting and satisfying customers.&#160;</li>\n<li>If you're creating an online business, get creative and diversify your marketing efforts using SEO, photography, social media, and specialized content.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The global health crisis has accelerated the growth from brick-and-mortar stores to <a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/ecommerce\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ent-tags\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/ecommerce\">ecommerce</a>&#160;by five years, according to&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/ibm\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ai-metadata\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/ibm\">IBM</a>'s US Retail Index. In 2020 alone, ecommerce is expected to grow by nearly 20%.</p><p>While the idea of launching an&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/e-commerce\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ai-metadata\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/e-commerce\">ecommerce</a>&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/business\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ai-metadata\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/business\">business</a>&#160;is exciting, there is a lot to consider. Following these five tips, you'll be able to optimize your customers'&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/online-shopping\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ai-metadata\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/online-shopping\">online shopping</a> experience and, consequently, boost customer acquisition, retention, and conversion.&#160;</p><h2>Maximize user experience&#160;</h2><p>Maximize your resources on providing quality user experience (UX). With new features rolling out periodically on social and other platforms, consumers are creating new online buying habits. A constant UX maintenance is a must.</p><p>Getting customers to your store requires a lot of effort, and the customer journey must be seamless. Streamline user experience for all steps of customer journey.&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/article/354111\" target=\"_self\" rel=\"follow\">Twenty-eight percent of customers</a>&#160;don't follow through the purchase when the checkout process is too long or confusing. Visit your store and click around as if it's your first time. Are your best sellers easy to access with just a few clicks? Conduct analyses on keyword search and pages. Which keywords bring customers to your store? What are the most visited pages? Quality UX will increase retention and conversion rates for your business.&#160;</p><h2>A picture is worth a thousand words</h2><p><a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/search-engine-optimization\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ai-metadata\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/search-engine-optimization\">Search engine optimization</a>&#160;(SEO) is crucial for any ecommerce operation. Often, what sets apart one seller from the other is a great cover photo, especially when your product or service is competitive on the e-commerce platform.</p><p>Product imagery is a big trend now that social channels offer in-app shopping features, such as <a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/instagram\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ai-metadata\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/instagram\">Instagram</a>&#160;Shopping.&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/pinterest\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ai-metadata\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/pinterest\">Pinterest</a>'s visual search tool allows consumers to find a product from a picture.&#160;</p><p>Businesses need product-only images for catalogs and product-related images for the website and&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/marketing\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ai-metadata\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/marketing\">marketing</a>&#160;campaigns. These pictures are a great investment as you can use them across multiple&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/sales\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ai-metadata\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/sales\">sales</a>&#160;channels. You could hire a professional or learn&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/article/354875\" target=\"_self\" rel=\"follow\">ecommerce product photography</a>&#160;on your own. Whichever option you take, have some basic knowledge about the essential tools<strong>&#160;</strong>for product photography.</p><h2>Encourage social buying to diversify storefronts&#160;</h2><p>Since March, stay-at-home orders have been on the rise, and so has social buying. Consumers discuss products on forum sites and vouch for services to their social followers.</p><p>Connect with fans on social channels to encourage social buying and diversify your storefronts. Fans will discover your business and make a purchase on social, sometimes without even visiting your shop at all.&#160;</p><p>Social platforms are a great place to promote your brand. It's where new products and services are discovered daily. A healthy amount of social followers and search engine optimized contents will help your brand shine in the long run.</p><p>When delegating tasks, ensure a close collaboration between the marketing or PR team that manages social accounts and the&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/customer-service\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ai-metadata\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/customer-service\">customer service</a> team. Streamline communications so that the questions, concerns, and complaints collected by the marketing team are addressed by the customer experience team.</p><h2>Get creative with cutting-edge technology&#160;</h2><p>Retailers could consider providing Augmented Reality (AR) based try-on tools.&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/sephora\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ai-metadata\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/sephora\">Sephora</a>'s AR tool allows you to try on multiple shades of lipstick.&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/ikea\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ai-metadata\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/ikea\">IKEA</a>&#160;lets you preview furniture in your space on your smartphone.</p><p>Virtual Reality (VR) store visits and&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/qr-codes\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ai-metadata\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/qr-codes\">QR codes</a>&#160;are other options. When shipping products to customers, send along a QR code which introduces more about the product, such as product updates or customer-sourced content about your service.</p><h2>Create and build content for your business</h2><p>A good content marketing strategy will drive traffic, lower the cost of acquisition, and provide valuable evergreen content that will be read for years to come. Unlike pay per click search ads or display ads, creating quality content doesn't cost anything. Research your competitors, listen to your customers, and highlight great user experience.&#160;</p><p>What are they already saying about your brand on social media? Can you find an honest fan review to highlight? Explore the social channels to determine best practices for each. Standardize the content creation process for ease of scheduling. Lastly, use multiple content formats to diversify traffic: blog posts, videos, social posts, webinars, and podcasts — the list goes on.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 23:59:06","updatedTime":"2020-10-19 23:59:06","title":"5 things mentally strong people do in work and life that seem counterintuitive (but they're not)","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/5-things-mentally-strong-people-do-that-seem-counterintuitive-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ed1474c3f7370121906c054?format=jpeg\" alt=\"woman working at a table\" height=\"1414\" width=\"2121\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Mentally strong people eliminate distractions, reflect on their mistakes, and know when to quit.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kelvin Murray/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/author/amy-morin\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\" data-uri=\"fa86f4bd4d935d709a1e8684bd64a05c\">Amy Morin</a>&#160;is a psychotherapist, licensed clinical social worker, mental strength coach, and international bestselling author.</li>\n<li>While some people might make decisions that seem counterintuitive to being strong, Morin explains these choices are critical to building mental strength.</li>\n<li>Mentally strong people know when to quit, slow down, ask for help, change their work environments, and embrace their emotions.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Just like you shouldn't judge a book by the cover, you shouldn't determine if someone is mentally strong just by observing their behavior at work. After all, you never know what sort of internal battles someone might be fighting.</p><p>Additionally, on the surface, some of the behaviors <a href=\"https://amymorinlcsw.com/mentally-strong-people-podcast/\">mentally strong people</a> exhibit might get confused for weakness, rather than strength. In fact, some of their choices might even seem counterintuitive at first glance. But here's the reason behind some of those choices they make.</p><h2><strong style=\"color: #000000;\">1. They alter their environment</strong></h2><p>When you see someone hide the candy dish at their desk, your first thought might be, \"They must not have any willpower.\" But the truth is, resources like willpower are in limited supply no matter how strong you are.</p><p>Mentally strong people want to reserve those resources for the most important battles in life. They set their lives up in a way that ensures they won't have to constantly fight temptation all day long.</p><p>Mental strength isn't about being able to tolerate pain and endure extreme discomfort without flinching. Instead, it's often about choosing which battles you want to fight.</p><h2><strong style=\"color: #000000;\">2. They carve out time to reflect</strong></h2><p>You might imagine a strong person doesn't need to take time to think — after all, they're busy doing important things.</p><p>But mentally strong people know their mindset matters. Whether they're reflecting on their mistakes so they can learn from them, or they're creating new career goals for themselves, they set aside time to think.</p><p>No matter how busy they are, they make time to reflect on their lives. In fact, the busier they are, the more time they may need to think about how to ensure their priorities are in line with their values.</p><h2><strong style=\"color: #000000;\">3. They quit</strong></h2><p>People who don't understand mental strength sometimes say things like, \"mentally strong people never give up.\" That's not true though.</p><p>People who are acting tough might finish a race on a broken ankle. But strong people know when to quit. They set aside their egos and throw in the towel quite often.</p><p>When they discover that the effort to reach a goal isn't in line with their values, they might abandon their goal. For example, if family's a top priority, they might quit a side hustle that interferes with family time.</p><p>Or, if they realize a goal is going to require 100% of their attention and that goal is third on the priority list, they might quit. Then, they have even more energy to focus on their main priorities and other goals.</p><p>They know they're strong enough to handle any criticism they might get for \"quitting\" and they are open-minded enough to change their opinions.</p><h2><strong style=\"color: #000000;\">4. They ask for help</strong></h2><p>Mentally strong people know they don't have all the answers. They aren't concerned with trying to prove to everyone that they're completely self-reliant all the time.</p><p>They ask for help when they need it. Whether that means going to therapy before work to ensure they're taking care of their mental health or it means asking a friend for some financial or job advice, they recognize that other people have skills, knowledge, and resources that can help them. And they don't feel insecure acknowledging that.</p><h2><strong style=\"color: #000000;\">5. They embrace their emotions</strong></h2><p>You might hear someone say something like, \"She's so strong. She didn't even cry at the funeral.\" But emotional suppression isn't a sign of strength. After all, it takes more strength to acknowledge and express your emotions than it does to mask them.</p><p>Mentally strong people embrace emotions — even the uncomfortable ones. They know it's okay to feel sad, angry, and scared. Rather than escape those emotions, they turn to healthy coping skills to manage them.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 23:59:06","updatedTime":"2020-10-19 23:59:06","title":"NASA gave Nokia $14.1 million to build a 4G network on the moon","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/nasa-nokia-4g-network-moon-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f8d7afc9e9fe4001900a014?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Astronaut planet phone\" height=\"2652\" width=\"3536\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Westend61/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Telecom equipment supplier Nokia is building a 4G network on the moon to help astronauts control lunar rovers, navigate lunar geography in real time, and stream videos.</li>\n<li>NASA gave Nokia-owned Bell Labs a $14.1 million grant for the project as part of its plans to establish a human presence on the moon by 2030.</li>\n<li>Bell Labs will upgrade the network to 5G in the future, though it didn't give a timescale for the project.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Telecom equipment supplier Nokia will use a $14.1 million grant to build <a href=\"https://twitter.com/BellLabs/status/1316780503358492674?s=20\">the moon's first wireless network</a> as part of NASA's plans to establish a human presence there.</p><p>NASA is investing the money in Nokia-owned American research company Bell Labs, which will build the 4G-LTE network, it said on Wednesday, October 14.</p><p>The improved <a href=\"https://twitter.com/BellLabs/status/1316780505203965959?s=20\">data transmission</a> will help astronauts control lunar rovers, navigate lunar geography in real time, and stream videos.</p><p>The mission ultimately will help show whether it's possible to have \"human habitation on the moon,\" <a href=\"https://twitter.com/BellLabs/status/1316780509599543296?s=20\">Bell Labs said</a>.</p><p>The initial 4G network will be upgraded to 5G in the future, it <a href=\"https://twitter.com/BellLabs/status/1316780503358492674?s=20\">said</a>. It is working with spaceflight engineering company Intuitive Machines on the project.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/the-altman-brothers-launch-apollo-to-invest-in-moonshot-companies-2020-7\">'Moonshot' startups to get a boost from new Apollo fund founded by former Y Combinator president Sam Altman and his 2 brothers</a></em></p><p>The network will be adapted to the moon's unique climate, and will be able to withstand extreme temperatures, radiation, and even rocket landings and launches, which vibrate the moon's surface.</p><p>The moon's 4G network will also use significantly smaller cells than those on Earth, Bell Labs said. These will have a smaller range, but they require less power and are easier to transport.</p><p>Neither NASA nor Bell Labs gave a timescale for the project.</p><h2>NASA invested $370 million in projects to support life on the moon</h2><p>The investment is part of NASA's \"Tipping Point\" scheme, which funds lunar tech developments for its \"Artemis\" program. The investments will help NASA meet its goals of sending the first woman and next man to the moon in 2024, having a lunar base on the moon by 2028, and establishing a sustainable presence there by 2030.</p><p>In the fifth and highest-value \"Tipping Point\" funding round to date, NASA gave more than $370 million to 14 US companies across nine states.</p><p>The companies must contribute some of the total project cost, <a href=\"https://www.nasa.gov/press-release/nasa-announces-partners-to-advance-tipping-point-technologies-for-the-moon-mars\">NASA said</a>. Combining NASA resources with industry contributions \"shepherds the development of critical space technologies while also saving the agency, and American taxpayers, money.\"</p><p>NASA invested $106 million in what it calls \"lunar surface innovation initiative technology,\" which helps humans and robots explore more of the moon. These include a fast, wireless charging system, a chemical heat and electrical power source that can survive extreme temperatures, and Nokia's 4G network.</p><p>NASA also invested around $256 million in cryogenic fluid management tech — liquefied gases kept at very low temperatures. These are essential for establishing a sustainable presence on the moon and enabling crewed missions to Mars, NASA said.</p><p>This included a $53 million investment in Tesla CEO Elon Musk's company SpaceX.</p><p>\"Together, NASA and industry are building up an array of mission-ready capabilities to support a sustainable presence on the Moon and future human missions to Mars,\" <a href=\"https://www.nasa.gov/press-release/nasa-announces-partners-to-advance-tipping-point-technologies-for-the-moon-mars\">Jim Bridenstine</a>, an administrator at NASA, said.</p><div It's the place that money moves into when people get nervous about the state of the world,\" he said in an interview Sunday with <a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/videos/tv/2020/10/18/exp-gps-1018-larry-summers-covid-economic-cost-16-trillion-dollars.cnn\">CNN's Fareed Zakaria</a>.&#160;</p><p>The former World Bank economist said that as long as the US political system isn't disrupted, \"the dollar's going to be okay.\"</p><p>Summers, who has also been an advisor to President Barack Obama and the Treasury chief for President Bill Clinton, noted that it is \"right to worry\" about the United States' handling of the coronavirus and its rising debt-load.&#160;</p><p>But, according to him, a near-zero interest rate environment means credit is cheap and the government can afford to borrow more and pay back what it owes.</p><p>\"The fact that we've got an interest rate that's essentially zero is telling us that the funds are available, and they're not going to crowd out anything important. Instead, they're going to push the economy forward,\" he said.</p><p><strong><em>Read More:</em></strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-market-crash-3-nonsensical-narratives-dangerous-heights-peter-cecchini-2020-10\"><em>An ex-Wall Street chief strategist lambasts 3 'nonsensical narratives' he says are pushing stocks to dangerous heights — and warns that the current rally is unsustainable</em></a></p><p>Instead of lending money to credit-worthy corporations, the higher priority should be to support unemployed, lower-income families, he said. \"All of the dangers are on the side of spending too little right now, rather than spending too much,\" he said.</p><p>Summers also noted the cost of COVID-19 testing is trivial compared to the cost of premature fatalities. Getting a test costs only about 1% of the $16 trillion dollars that the pandemic would end up costing the economy, he said.</p><p>\"The cost of incompetence here dwarfs the human cost of the Vietnam War in terms of fatalities that could have been avoided in terms of financial costs,\" Summers said.&#160;</p><p>Negotiations over a new set of stimulus measures are currently stalled, as Republicans and Democrats continue to wrangle over the details of the bill. While the White House hasn't yet officially upped its $1.8 trillion counteroffer to Pelosi's $2.2 trillion proposal, President Donald Trump repeated calls for a deal larger than the two options.</p><p><strong>Here's where US indexes stood at 11:55 a.m. ET on Monday:</strong></p><ul><li><strong><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/s&p_500?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestarkets&#38;utm_medium=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">S&#38;P 500</a>:</strong> 3,473.09, down 0.5%</li><li><strong><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/dow_jones?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestts&#38;utm_medium=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Dow Jones industrial average</a>:</strong> 28,528.50, down 0.3% (77 points)</li><li><strong><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/nasdaq_composite?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestts&#38;utm_medium=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Nasdaq composite</a>:</strong> 11,649.42, down 0.2%</li></ul><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-to-buy-etf-strategy-cathie-wood-ark-invest-2020-10\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Cathie Wood runs 5 funds that more than doubled broader market returns in the 3rd quarter. analyst","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/apple-iphone-12-preorders-release-double-iphone-11-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f85e24491aa9e001880b4fc?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Apple iPhone 12 Event October\" height=\"1462\" width=\"2778\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>iPhone 12\n<p class=\"copyright\">Apple</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Preorders for the iPhone 12 have more than doubled those of the iPhone 11, according to analyst Ming-Chi Kuo.</li>\n<li>Apple is said to have sold between 1.7 million and 2 million units of the iPhone 12 in its first 24 hours of preorder availability.&#160;</li>\n<li>The iPhone 11, comparatively, is said to have reached between 500,000 and 800,000 orders during the same period.</li>\n<li>For the full weekend, however, preorders fell slightly under the iPhone 11's, according to the estimates. But Apple is also launching the iPhone 12 in two new sizes next month that could see increased sales.</li>\n<li>Analysts have expected the iPhone 12 to be Apple's biggest smartphone launch in years, potentially resulting in a \"supercycle\" of upgrades.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Apple's iPhone 12 hasn't officially launched yet, but preorder estimates suggest the company's new smartphone lineup is off to a strong start.</p><p>Preorders for the iPhone 12 have more than doubled that of the iPhone 11 line in its first 24 hours of preorder availability, according to TF International Securities analyst Ming-Chi Kuo. The analyst, who has a reputation for reporting accurate details on upcoming Apple product launches, shared his findings in a research note reported by <a href=\"https://9to5mac.com/2020/10/19/iphone-12-preorders/\">9to5Mac</a>, <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2020/10/19/iphone-12-pre-orders-sales-exceed-iphone-11-top-analyst-says.html\">CNBC</a>, and <a href=\"https://appleinsider.com/articles/20/10/19/initial-iphone-12-and-iphone-12-pro-pre-order-results-best-iphone-11-kuo-says\">Apple Insider</a>.</p><p>Apple sold between 1.7 million and 2 million iPhone 12 units during the phone's first day of preorders on October 16, according to Kuo. The iPhone 11, by comparison, sold between 500,000 and 800,000 units in the same time period. Apple <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/apple-stop-disclosing-iphone-ipad-mac-unit-sales-quarter-2018-11?r=UK\">stopped reporting iPhone sales numbers</a> in late 2018.&#160;</p><p>For the full weekend, however, Kuo predicted that iPhone 12 preorders fell slightly lower at around 9 million units compared to the iPhone 11's 12 million, as CNBC noted. But Apple is also launching the iPhone 12 in two new sizes next month.&#160;</p><p>Kuo also reported that the more premium iPhone 12 Pro model saw higher demand than expected. The iPhone 12 Pro, which starts at $1,000, comes with a few extra features not found on the standard iPhone 12, such as a telephoto camera lens, a LiDAR sensor for detecting depth, options for additional storage, and the ability to shoot portrait shots in Night Mode among other differences.&#160;</p><p>Preorders for the iPhone 12 and iPhone 12 Pro began on October 16, with general availability coming on October 23. The iPhone 12 Mini and iPhone 12 Pro Max are up for preorder starting November 6 and officially launch on November 13.</p><p>The iPhone 12, which Apple <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/watch-apple-event-october-live-blog-iphone-12-homepod-announcements-2020-10\">unveiled on October 13</a>, comes with a refreshed design with flat edges, support for 5G, an improved camera that should be better at taking photos in the dark, new color options, and a faster processor. Apple also launched a new magnetic MagSafe wireless charger for its new iPhone 12 lineup.&#160;</p><p>The iPhone 12 is expected to represent a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/apple-iphone-12-release-most-important-product-launch-in-years-2020-10\">\"supercycle\" of upgrades for Apple,</a> which has grappled with slowing iPhone sales in recent years. The combination of 5G support, the notion that many active iPhones in use are now several years old, and new size options could incentivize consumers to upgrade, analysts have said.</p><p>Wedbush analyst Daniel Ives has previously said he expects the iPhone 12 launch to be the most significant iPhone launch cycle for Apple since the iPhone 6 and iPhone 6 Plus debuted in 2014.</p><p>Those phones, however, <a href=\"https://finance.yahoo.com/news/apple-receives-record-pre-orders-130255260.html\">reached 4 million in preorders</a> in their first 24 hours of availability, according to Kuo as 9to5Mac reports. But it's important to remember that the range of between 1.7 million and 2 million preorders that Kuo estimates for the iPhone 12 does not include the iPhone 12 Mini or iPhone 12 Pro Max.</p><p>When the iPhone 12 and iPhone 12 Pro went up for preorder on October 16, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/iphone-12-pre-order-error-reports-apple-t-mobile-verizon-2020-10\">some customers encountered errors</a> on the websites for Apple, Verizon, and T-Mobile, although it's unclear if those hiccups were the result of high demand or a separate issue.&#160;&#160;</p><div David Perdue</strong> for the US Senate election in Georgia this November.&#160;&#160;</p><h2><strong>The candidates</strong></h2><p>Ossoff is an investigative journalist, business owner, and Georgia native. Before running for US Senate, he was the 2017 Democratic nominee for the high-profile special election in Georgia's 6th District, which he ultimately lost. Ossoff launched his US Senate campaign in September 2019, and cleared the competitive primary field to avoid a runoff for the nomination on June 9.</p><p>Ossoff's <a href=\"https://electjon.com/policy/\">campaign platform</a> emphasizes expanding access to affordable healthcare and protecting Social Security, combatting climate change and investing in green infrastructure, and supporting small businesses.&#160;</p><p>Perdue, <a href=\"https://perduesenate.com/meet-david/\">a wealthy businessman and consultant</a> who previously served as the CEO of Reebok and chair and CEO of Dollar General, was first elected in 2014, and is now running for a second term. In Congress, Perdue serves on the Committees on Armed Services, Banking, Housing, and Urban Affairs, Budget, and Foreign Relations.&#160;</p><p>While Perdue hasn't been as much of a firebrand as some other GOP Senators up for reelection this year, <a href=\"https://www.perdue.senate.gov/about/david\">his official Senate website</a> touts that he is an \"early supporter of President Donald J. Trump and continues to be one of the President's closest allies in the US Senate.\" He's voted in lockstep with Trump 95% of the time since 2017, <a href=\"https://projects.fivethirtyeight.com/congress-trump-score/david-perdue/\">according to FiveThirtyEight.&#160;</a></p><h2><strong>The stakes</strong></h2><p>In addition to winning back the White House, regaining control of the US Senate for the first time since 2015 is a top priority for Democrats and would be a major accomplishment towards either delivering on a future president Joe Biden's policy goals or thwarting President Donald Trump's second-term agenda.&#160;</p><p>Currently, the US Senate is made up of 53 Republicans, 45 Democrats, and two independents that caucus with Democrats, winning that Democrats need to win back a net total of four seats to have a 51-seat majority (if Biden wins, his vice president would also serve as president of the Senate and would be a tie-breaker vote).&#160;</p><p>And now, the US Senate is gearing up for a high-stakes confirmation battle to replace Justice Ruth Bader Ginsburg, who died at age 87 from pancreatic cancer on September 18. Within hours of her death, Senate Majority Leader Mitch McConnell of Kentucky pledged that Trump's nominee for the high court <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mcconnell-confirms-senate-will-vote-on-ruth-bader-ginsburg-replacement-2020-9\">would receive a vote on the floor of the Senate</a>, and Trump said the day after that <a href=\"https://twitter.com/realDonaldTrump/status/1307321159113936896\">he would name a replacement \"without delay.\"&#160;</a></p><p>Ginsburg's death threw a stick of dynamite into an already supercharged election shaped by a deadly pandemic that has so far claimed over 200,000 American lives, and a national reckoning around race after several high-profile deaths of Black Americans in encounters with police.&#160;</p><p>Trump and McConnell's posturing on the issue has excited conservatives enthusiastic about the possibility of Trump getting to appoint a third justice in his first term, but infuriated liberals <a href=\"https://www.motherjones.com/2020-elections/2020/09/mcconnell-hypocrisy-supreme-court-confirmation-ruth-bader-ginsburg/\">who accused McConnell of blatant hypocrisy </a>after he refused to hold confirmation proceedings for Obama's Supreme Court nominee Merrick Garland in 2016, citing the upcoming presidential election. Senate Republicans held the seat open long enough for Trump to appoint his choice, Justice Neil Gorsuch, to the seat.&#160;</p><p>McConnell's quest to confirm a new justice before the end of Trump's first term puts the chamber on a collision course with the reelection hopes of many vulnerable Republican Senators, including Perdue.&#160;</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Jon Ossoff  (@ossoff) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1307847018237263873?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">September 21, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>&#160;</p><p>While Georgia has been considered a safe Republican stronghold for decades, the tide in the state is shifting in Democrats' favor thanks to <a href=\"http://centerforpolitics.org/crystalball/articles/states-of-play-georgia/\">the fast-expanding Atlanta metro area.</a></p><p>The counties surrounding Atlanta, <a href=\"http://centerforpolitics.org/crystalball/articles/states-of-play-georgia/\">including Cobb and Gwinnett counties</a>, have been rapidly gaining population and trending towards Democrats in recent election cycles. And the confluence of Trump's unpopularity and the pandemic — which has hit Georgia hard — could make the state even more competitive than ever.&#160;</p><p>Both the Biden and Trump campaigns <a href=\"https://www.ajc.com/politics/politics-blog/joe-biden-unveils-senior-leadership-team-in-georgia/MPVQWIF44FHIPHWPTYBNBZR6UI/\">are also investing big in Georgia</a>, another indication of how the COVID-19 pandemic has shifted the electoral college map towards Democrats. Trump now leads Democratic nominee Joe Biden by just 1.3 points on average in polls of the state, <a href=\"https://projects.fivethirtyeight.com/polls/president-general/georgia/\">according to FiveThirtyEight's polling averages.&#160;</a></p><p>Georgia has two US Senate elections in 2020. In addition to the Ossoff-Purdue race, Sen. <strong>Kelly Loeffler</strong> is running for a full term in a jungle special election where candidates from both parties compete on the same ballot and the top two advance to a runoff. Loeffler was appointed to serve out the rest of former Sen. Johnny Isakson's term after Isakson resigned his seat due to health problems in December 2019.&#160;</p><h2><strong>The money race</strong></h2><p>Ossoff has proven himself to be a talented fundraiser in this election and in his 2017 race. While he started out his general election race against Perdue at a significant cash disadvantage, he's quickly worked to make up the gap.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.opensecrets.org/races/summary?cycle=2020&id=GAS1&spec=Np;spec=N\">According to the Center for Responsive Politics</a>, Ossoff has raised $28.1 million, spent $19.8 million, and has $8.3 million in cash on hand as of September 30. Meanwhile, Perdue has raised $20 million, spent $11.9 million, and has $8.1 million in cash on hand.&#160;</p><p>In 2020's third fundraising quarter, Ossoff <a href=\"https://www.augustachronicle.com/news/20201016/jon-ossoff-sets-quarterly-fundraising-record-for-senate-candidate-from-georgia\">brought in an impressive haul of $21.3 million</a>, a haul that came out to three times more than the $7 million Perdue's campaign raised in the same timeframe.&#160;</p><h2><strong style=\"color: #000000;\">What the polling says</strong></h2><p>The most recent polls <a href=\"https://projects.fivethirtyeight.com/polls/senate/georgia/\">show a tight race between Perdue and Ossoff</a> with many results within the margin of error. Perdue leads Ossoff by just 1.3 percentage points on average <a href=\"https://www.realclearpolitics.com/epolls/2020/senate/ga/georgia_senate_perdue_vs_ossoff-7067.html\">in RealClearPolitics' polling averages.&#160;</a></p><p>A recent poll of the race <a href=\"http://www.surveyusa.com/client/PollReport.aspx?g=b396b793-781d-4382-9ada-fc4cc50dacb6\">conducted by SurveyUSA</a> October 8-12 found Perdue leading Ossoff by three points, 46% to 43%, among likely voter. Another poll <a href=\"https://poll.qu.edu/georgia/release-detail?ReleaseID=3679\">conducted by Quinnipiac University</a> found Ossoff ahead of Perdue by six points, 51% 5o 45%, among likely voters, <a href=\"https://filesforprogress.org/memos/2020-senate-project/week-4/toplines/psp_ga_special_week_4_toplines.pdf\">while a Data for Progress survey</a> found Ossoff leading Perdue by a smaller margin of one point, 44% to 43%, among likely voters.&#160;</p><h2><strong>What some of the experts say</strong></h2><p>The <a href=\"https://cookpolitical.com/ratings/senate-race-ratings\">Cook Political Report</a> rates the race as a tossup,&#160; <a href=\"https://insideelections.com/ratings/senate\">Inside Elections</a> rates it tilts Republican, and <a href=\"http://centerforpolitics.org/crystalball/2020-senate/\">Sabato's Crystal Ball at the University of Virginia Center for Politics</a> rate the race as leans Republican.</p><p>According to <a href=\"https://projects.fivethirtyeight.com/2020-election-forecast/senate/georgia/\">FiveThirtyEight</a>, Perdue has a 72% chance of defeating Ossoff in the November election and is expected to receive 51% of the popular vote.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a (Grace Panetta,Madison Hall)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5949f16be592ed34008b5cc4?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn60@2020_5/2020/10/19/15-59-48-267_b68d9c0587f00446.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn56@2020_5/2020/10/19/15-59-47-418_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=10DU2z-lCKM:cacUNYsXxnk:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn59@2020_4/2020/10/19/15-59-47-471_84545ac2919a2e57.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=10DU2z-lCKM:cacUNYsXxnk:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn44@2020_3/2020/10/19/15-59-46-573_81fb059a044c1529.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn91@2020_5/2020/10/19/15-59-43-999_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=10DU2z-lCKM:cacUNYsXxnk:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn39@2020_1/2020/10/19/15-59-42-792_4bcd0a3b5457ff91.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/10DU2z-lCKM":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn7@2020_6/2020/10/19/15-59-45-659_4e58fc8fcb0b8443.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1603123145999},{"createdTime":"2020-10-19 23:59:05","updatedTime":"2020-10-19 23:59:05","title":"The arrest of Mexico's former defense minister on drug charges reveals a sinister reality about the drug war","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/salvador-cienfuegos-reveals-corruption-in-mexican-military-in-drug-war-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f8cd2f2c21cfb0019468aa6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Mexico Enrique Pena Nieto Salvador Cienfuegos Zepeda Vidal Francisco Soberon Sanz\" height=\"1249\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Gen. Salvador Cienfuegos, center, then Mexico&#39;s defense minister, at a ceremony in Mexico City with President Enrique Peña Nieto, left, September 19, 2018.\n<p class=\"copyright\">REUTERS/Daniel Becerril</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>On October 15, US authorities arrested former Mexican Defense Minister Salvador Cienfuegos as he arrived at at Los Angeles' international airport.</li>\n<li>The arrest of a former official of Cienfuegos' stature is unprecedented, and it may yield the strongest evidence yet that Mexico's military, which has lead the fight against that country's cartels, is&#160;thoroughly corrupted.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The US arrest of Mexico's former defense minister on drug charges confirms what has been alleged by traffickers themselves: That the country's military, which plays an outsized role in the fight against organized crime, has been thoroughly corrupted.</p><p>On October 15, the US Ambassador to Mexico, Christopher Landau, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/m_ebrard/status/1316922881247485954\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">informed</a> Foreign Minister Marcelo Ebrard that former general Salvador Cienfuegos Zepeda, Mexico's defense secretary under former President Enrique Peña Nieto (2012-2018), had been arrested at Los Angeles' international airport.</p><p>The arrest order from the US Drug Enforcement Administration (DEA) came after Cienfuegos — dubbed \"El Padrino,\" or the \"Godfather\" — was charged with three counts of drug conspiracy and one count of money laundering, according to <a href=\"https://www.yumpu.com/en/document/read/64591557/cienfuegos-indictment\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">an indictment filed</a> in August 2019 in the Eastern District of New York.</p><p>The charges stem from allegations that he colluded with the H-2 Cartel between 2015 and 2017, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/keegan_hamilton/status/1317150145574830080\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">according to court documents</a>. The H-2 Cartel — which has its roots in the Beltrán Leyva Organization — was formerly led by Juan Francisco Patrón Sánchez, alias \"H2,\" who was <a href=\"https://www.insightcrime.org/news/brief/death-blo-leader-illustrates-marines-decisive-role-underworld-fight/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">shot and killed</a> by Mexican Marines in early 2017.</p><p>US federal prosecutors accuse the former general of using his \"public position to help the H-2 Cartel … operate with impunity\" in exchange for bribes, according to <a href=\"https://twitter.com/keegan_hamilton/status/1317150145574830080/photo/1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">an October 16 letter</a> from prosecutors to Eastern District judge Carol B. Amon.</p><p>Evidence cited includes<a href=\"https://twitter.com/keegan_hamilton/status/1317150145574830080/photo/3\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> </a>\"thousands of [intercepted] Blackberry Messenger communications\" that allegedly show Cienfuegos shielded the group from military operations, secured maritime transport of drug shipments, warned the group about US law enforcement investigations and introduced its members to other corrupt Mexican officials, prosecutors said.</p><p>Cienfuegos' assistance ensured the H-2 Cartel operated without \"significant interference from the Mexican military,\" allowing the crime group to import \"thousands of kilograms of cocaine, heroin, marijuana and methamphetamine into the United States,\" prosecutors alleged in the letter.</p><p>Cienfuegos is not the first Mexican official accused of conspiring with the H-2 Cartel. Former Nayarit state attorney general Edgar Veytia was <a href=\"https://www.insightcrime.org/news/brief/mexico-attorney-general-arrested-us-spotlights-new-links-authorities-crime/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">arrested in 2017</a> and later <a href=\"https://www.justice.gov/opa/pr/former-mexican-state-attorney-general-sentenced-20-years-prison-participation-international\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">sentenced to 20 years</a> in jail for his role in an international drug trafficking conspiracy with the group.</p><p>While Cienfuegos is the highest-ranking member of Mexico's military to face drug charges, he is <a href=\"https://www.insightcrime.org/news/analysis/mexico-security-official-drug-charges/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">just the latest</a> top-level security official to be arrested.</p><p>Genaro García Luna, Mexico's secretary of public security from 2006 to 2012, was indicted in 2019 on a number of <a href=\"https://www.insightcrime.org/news/analysis/us-overlooked-rogue-officials-mexico/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">cocaine trafficking charges.</a> He and two high-ranking police officers that worked under him, Luis Cárdenas Palomino and Ramón Pequeño García, were also accused of accepting bribes from the Sinaloa Cartel.</p><h3>InSight Crime analysis</h3><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f8cd2e99e9fe40019009faa?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Mexico Salvador Cienfuegos Jim Mattis\" height=\"1666\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>US Defense Secretary Jim Mattis with Cienfuegos at a welcome ceremony in Mexico City, September 15, 2017.\n<p class=\"copyright\">REUTERS/Edgard Garrido</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Cienfuegos' arrest is unprecedented. That it even happened at all is remarkable.</p><p>Military officials have long been accused of corruption but are rarely, if ever, prosecuted. It has been more than two decades since former general and anti-drug czar Jesús Gutiérrez Rebollo was <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/1997/03/18/world/another-mexican-general-is-arrested-and-charged-with-links-to-drug-cartel.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">arrested and later convicted</a> for colluding with high-profile cocaine traffickers like Amado Carrillo Fuentes, better known as the \"Lord of the Skies.\"</p><p>Cienfuegos' arrest also hits hard Mexico's armed forces, which became even more central to attacking organized crime groups when in 2006 then-President Felipe Calderón launched an official crackdown. The militarized approach has only ballooned in the ensuing so-called drug war.</p><p>Since then, more than 200,000 people have been killed in Mexico, and tens of thousands more have disappeared. The indictment suggests that while Cienfuegos was leading the institution at the heart of the fight against organized crime under the Peña Nieto administration, he was also allegedly colluding with the very criminals he pledged to root out.</p><p>Indeed, Cienfuegos' arrest further upends any notion of a \"war,\" in which the state is on one side and criminal groups on the other. In reality, these actors are much more intertwined, maintaining order and driving violence as a means to regulate conditions that are mutually beneficial.</p><p>The United States has much to answer for as well. With the arrest of García Luna and now Cienfuegos, it has become increasingly clear that US security and government officials frequently work with counterparts deeply involved in the drug trade. The question now is what was known and when. Speculation about high-level corruption has swirled for decades, especially during the Calderón administration's tenure from 2006 to 2012.</p><p>\"There were a number of red flags when Cienfuegos was a general, and when he was named defense minister in 2012, I had heard rumors about his corruption,\" Mike Vigil, the DEA's former Chief of International Operations, told InSight Crime.</p><p>This is far from the first time Cienfuegos has been at the center of controversy. In 2015, the former army chief <a href=\"https://www.vice.com/en/article/mbn7an/soldiers-wont-be-treated-like-criminals-in-ayotzinapa-case-mexico-army-chief-says\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">infamously said</a> that his soldiers \"won't be treated like criminals\" in relation to the forced disappearance of 43 students from the Ayotzinapa Normal School. Last month, authorities <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/us-mexico-human-rights-ayotzinapa/arrest-warrants-issued-against-mexican-military-members-in-2014-student-disappearances-idUSKBN26H0RP\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">issued arrest warrants</a> for the alleged material and intellectual authors of the crime, including members of the military.</p><p>In 2014, Cienfuegos also <a href=\"https://english.elpais.com/elpais/2015/02/20/inenglish/1424442625_945153.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">rejected accusations</a> that his troops were culpable in the so-called <a href=\"https://www.insightcrime.org/news/brief/mexican-govt-confirms-massacre-army-tlatlaya/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Tlatlaya massacre, </a>when soldiers killed 22 people in what was described as a \"shootout.\" In reality, the soldiers received a <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/jul/03/mexican-soldiers-ordered-to-kill-in-san-pedro-limon-claim-rights-activists\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">direct order to kill</a>, according to <a href=\"https://www.wola.org/2015/07/in-mexicos-tlatlaya-massacre-soldiers-were-ordered-to-take-them-out/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">human rights activists</a>.</p><p>Cienfuegos' arrest also adds to the list of Mexican officials to be charged in the United States and not at home. As a result, he won't be held to account for some of the <a href=\"https://aristeguinoticias.com/0902/mexico/rigor-y-contundencia-ante-violaciones-a-derechos-humanos-por-militares-cienfuegos/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">grave human rights abuses</a> he is accused of overseeing as a general in Mexico.</p><p>What's more, the military continues to be one of Mexico's <a href=\"https://www.inegi.org.mx/contenidos/programas/ensu/doc/ensu2020_marzo_presentacion_ejecutiva.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">most trusted institutions</a> and a mainstay of domestic security. A <a href=\"https://www.dof.gob.mx/nota_detalle.php?codigo=5593105&fecha=11/05/20202020\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">May decree</a> signed earlier this year solidified its place in combatting crime groups for the foreseeable future. The United States also <a href=\"https://www.insightcrime.org/news/brief/us-mexico-hardline-drug-approach/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">recently urged</a> Mexico to crack down harder, demanding the Mexican government demonstrate its \"commitment to dismantling the cartels and their criminal enterprises.\"</p><p>This all but guarantees that the armed forces will remain on the frontlines, despite the latest headlines.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/salvador-cienfuegos-reveals-corruption-in-mexican-military-in-drug-war-2020-10'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a Britain and the EU to reach a compromise trade deal, according to a <a href=\"https://www.cbi.org.uk/media-centre/articles/covid-hit-businesses-call-for-pragmatic-approach-to-secure-historic-uk-eu-agreement-cbi-trade-associations/\">statement</a> from the Confederation of British Industry.</p><p>The groups involved come from a diverse range of industries including technology, financials, automotives, aviation, farming, pharmaceuticals, and chemicals. They said that securing a prompt trade agreement \"matters greatly for jobs and livelihoods.\"</p><p>The Confederation of British Industry, British Retail Consortium, TheCityUK, techUK, and the Society of Motor Manufacturers and Traders are some of the organizations that united to urge both sides to reach an agreement.</p><p>\"With compromise and tenacity, a deal can be done. Businesses call on leaders on both sides to find a route through,\" the groups said.</p><p><strong><em>Read More: </em></strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-to-buy-small-companies-recommendations-high-upside-rbc-2020-10\"><em>Buy these 7 unheralded stocks right now for near-term upside of at least 25% as growth accelerates to a new level, RBC says</em></a></p><p>The group of trade organizations, which represents about 7 million people, or close to 200,000 companies, said that an ambitious trade deal would impact business efforts to prepare for the end of the Brexit transition period later in December.</p><p>\"It will help investment by removing the threat of tariffs and quotas. And it will catalyse confidence through enhanced customs co-operation while making a precious data agreement possible, vital for services industries which make up 80 per cent of the UK economy.\"</p><p>\"With each day that passes, business resilience is chipped away,\" the groups said.</p><p>\"The UK's aerospace, defence, space and security industries will face major disruption without a deal, through delays to cross-border trade, costly administrative requirements and a new regulatory system,\" Paul Everitt, chief executive of ADS, said in a statement. \"Businesses in our sectors are facing a daily struggle to survive as a result of the Covid-19 crisis, which has put 30,000 aerospace jobs at risk.\"</p><p>Michael Gove, a senior British official, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/uk-minister-door-still-ajar-for-post-brexit-talks-with-eu-2020-10\">said on Monday</a> the door is still \"ajar\" for the European Union to hold post-Brexit talks if Brussels officials change their minds on some key points. His statement contrasted to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/boris-johnson-uk-heading-for-no-trade-deal-brexit-eu-2020-10\">Prime Minister Boris Johnson saying last week</a> that the UK must href=\"https://www.politico.com/news/2020/10/19/biden-revamp-fraying-intel-community-430090\">according to a new report from Politico</a>.&#160;</p><p>\"Does anyone want a malt?\" Trump reportedly said during the briefing, calling a waiter into the room. \"We have the best malts, you have to try them.\"</p><p>The highly classified briefing, which focused on Afghanistan, took place at Trump's New Jersey golf club several months into his presidency, according to Politico.</p><p>The White House did not immediately respond to a request for comment from Business Insider.</p><p>Trump has garnered a reputation as a president who has no patience for intelligence briefings. The president reportedly doesn't read the written intelligence reports he's given on a daily basis, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-looks-at-charts-in-intelligence-briefings-2020-5\">and prefers to look at visuals.</a></p><p>The president faced criticism over the summer after The New York Times <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/06/26/us/politics/russia-afghanistan-bounties.html\">reported</a> that US intelligence officials concluded Russia was paying bounties to Taliban-linked Afghan militants to kill US troops, and the Trump administration hadn't taken any known actions in response. The White House initially said Trump was never briefed on the intelligence, though multiple reports suggested otherwise.&#160;</p><p>In a <a href=\"https://www.axios.com/trump-russia-bounties-taliban-putin-call-4a0f6110-ab58-41c0-96fc-57b507462af1.html\">July interview with Axios</a>, Trump said he had not confronted Russian President Vladimir Putin over the intelligence assessment in a number of phone conversations.&#160;</p><p>The president's apparent disinterest in intelligence has also been pointed to as a major factor in his disastrous response to the coronavirus pandemic. Intelligence officials <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/coronavirus-all-the-times-trump-was-warned-about-pandemic-2020-3\">repeatedly warned Trump</a> of the threat of COVID-19 in the early months of 2020, but he ignored them and downplayed the virus to the US public.&#160;</p><p>\"The president didn't want to hear it,\" Trump's former national security adviser John Bolton <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/exclusive-interview-john-bolton-trump-impeachment-election-coronavirus-2020-8\">told Insider political correspondent Sonam Sheth in August.</a> \"He didn't want to hear bad news about his friend Xi Jinping — he didn't want to hear about the Chinese cover-up about what was actually happening with the virus in China.\"</p><p>Bolton said that Trump \"didn't want
