Duffy)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5ee8d61af0f4197e7e072f85?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn45@2020_2/2020/10/19/15-59-39-008_fb7759b333527bf6.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f2b31b62618b944fb2bf708?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn31@2020_2/2020/10/19/15-59-40-139_3cec9eb45c789361.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn56@2020_5/2020/10/19/15-59-47-418_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=naPl2LuSGfY:ClhG1ODqiCk:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn3@2020_4/2020/10/19/15-59-45-544_06f71f3c1e9dab0f.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=naPl2LuSGfY:ClhG1ODqiCk:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn55@2020_3/2020/10/19/15-59-42-216_8fe15cc2ba43140c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn91@2020_5/2020/10/19/15-59-43-999_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=naPl2LuSGfY:ClhG1ODqiCk:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn28@2020_6/2020/10/19/15-59-45-086_fba351e25aed2203.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/naPl2LuSGfY":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn80@2020_1/2020/10/19/15-59-49-216_14743372728cf349.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1603123145982},{"createdTime":"2020-10-19 23:59:06","updatedTime":"2020-10-19 23:59:06","title":"The oldest college in every US state","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/oldest-college-every-state-2018-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6e215c0f4d5500110325c3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"harvard\" height=\"2683\" width=\"3578\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Harvard University is the oldest college in the entire country — it dates back to 1636.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jay Yuan/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The oldest college in each US state includes some of the most prestigious academic institutions in the country and several flagship state universities.</li>\n<li>The oldest college in the United States is Harvard University, founded in 1636.</li>\n<li>Meanwhile, the most recent state to get a college for the first time is Alaska.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The United States is home to some pretty old colleges and universities.</p><p>In fact, there are more than a dozen that are older than America itself — none older than Harvard University, which was <a href=\"https://www.harvard.edu/about-harvard/harvard-glance/history\">founded in 1636</a>.</p><p>Meanwhile, other states took longer to open their first colleges. The most recent state to get its first college is Alaska, whose University of Alaska Fairbanks <a href=\"https://www.uaf.edu/centennial/\">celebrated its 100th anniversary</a> in 2017.</p><p>Across the US, the list of oldest colleges in each state features some of the most prestigious academic institutions in the country as well as flagship state universities and a handful of lesser-known schools.</p><p>Read on to find out the oldest college in every US state and Washington, DC.</p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tALABAMA: Spring Hill College in Mobile\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6a4d48ef332b0028c11905?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Spring Hill College alabama\" height=\"1411\" width=\"1882\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Spring Hill College.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Barry Winiker/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Spring Hill College in Mobile, Alabama, was founded in 1830 and claims to be Alabama's oldest institution of higher learning. According to <a href=\"https://www.shc.edu/about/history/\">the school's website</a>, it is the first Catholic college in the Southeast United States, the third-oldest Jesuit college, and the fifth-oldest Catholic college in the US.</p>\n\tALASKA: The University of Alaska Fairbanks in Fairbanks\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5bb3e2e19fb84c226a492f58?format=jpeg\" alt=\"university alaska fairbanka\" height=\"713\" width=\"951\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The University of Alaska Fairbanks.\n<p class=\"copyright\">UAF</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The University of Alaska Fairbanks celebrated its 100th anniversary in 2017. The university was founded in 1917, however, classes didn't officially open until 1922, according to <a href=\"https://uaf.edu/uaf/about/\">the school's website</a>. In 1935, the Alaska Agricultural College and School of Mines became the University of Alaska. The school awarded its first Ph.D. in 1955.</p>\n\tARIZONA: The University of Arizona in Tucson\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6ba9c0c4049200115cb3c1?format=jpeg\" alt=\"The University of Arizona\" height=\"2990\" width=\"3986\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The University of Arizona.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Katherine Welles/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The University of Arizona dates back to 1885, with enrollment at the school beginning in 1891. According to <a href=\"https://www.britannica.com/topic/University-of-Arizona\">Britannica</a>, in 1915, the university consisted of just three colleges &#8212; letters, arts, and sciences; mines and engineering; and agriculture. Today, there are <a href=\"https://www.arizona.edu/colleges-schools\">more than 15 colleges</a> for students to choose from.</p>\n\tARKANSAS: University of the Ozarks in Clarksville\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6baa9cc4049200115cb3ca?format=jpeg\" alt=\"the Ozark National Forest\" height=\"667\" width=\"889\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The Ozark National Forest.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Gunnar Rathbun/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><a href=\"https://ozarks.edu/about/history/\">The University of the Ozarks</a> in Clarksville, Arkansas, was founded in 1834 by Cumberland Presbyterian officials. The first classes were held in a two-room log schoolhouse. The name would eventually change from Cane Hill College to The College of the Ozarks and later The University of the Ozarks.&#160;</p><p>In 1957, The University of the Ozarks became the first traditionally white college in Arkansas to admit African American students, according to <a href=\"https://ozarks.edu/about/history/\">the school's website</a>.</p>\n\tCALIFORNIA: Santa Clara University in Santa Clara\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6baaf3c4049200115cb3d1?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Santa Clara University\" height=\"750\" width=\"1000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Santa Clara University.\n<p class=\"copyright\">jejim/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Santa Clara University in Santa Clara, California, was founded in 1851 as a preparatory school, though it has roots as a mission back to the late 1700s. In 1853, the school began offering collegiate courses.</p>\n\tCOLORADO: The University of Denver in Denver\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6bab86e3e76700117162d7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"university of denver\" height=\"666\" width=\"888\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The University of Denver.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Patrish Jackson/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The University of Denver dates back to 1864 when it was known as the Colorado Seminary. According to <a href=\"https://www.du.edu/about/history-traditions\">the university's website</a>, it was founded just six years after the founding of Denver City in what was then called the Colorado Territory. It later established one of the very first business schools in the entire country.</p>\n\tCONNECTICUT: Yale University in New Haven\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5b64bc08dcee301a008b4c9b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"yale university\" height=\"1332\" width=\"1776\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Yale University.\n<p class=\"copyright\">f11photo/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Yale University in New Haven, Connecticut, is one of America's oldest educational institutions &#8212; <a href=\"https://www.yale.edu/about-yale/traditions-history\">according to the university</a>, it has roots back to the 1640s, and became Yale College in 1718, 17 years after the Connecticut legislature adopted a charter to erect a Collegiate School.</p>\n\tDELAWARE: The University of Delaware in Newark\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6bac52c4049200115cb3e9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"University of Delaware newark\" height=\"1414\" width=\"1885\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The University of Delaware.\n<p class=\"copyright\">gregobagel/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The University of Delaware was founded in 1743, making it one of the oldest educational institutions in the country. <a href=\"https://www.udel.edu/about/history/#:~:text=One%20of%20the%20oldest%20universities,school%20in%20New%20London%2C%20Pennsylvania.\">According to the university's website</a>, a separate college opened in 1914 with 58 female students. In 1921, the two colleges merged to become the University of Delaware.</p>\n\tWASHINGTON, DC: Georgetown University in Washington, DC\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5b64afdc2be4ab1e008b4c97?format=jpeg\" alt=\"georgetown university\" height=\"1334\" width=\"1778\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Georgetown University.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Valerii Iavtushenko/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Georgetown University in Washington, DC, was founded in 1789. According to <a href=\"https://www.georgetown.edu/who-we-are/our-history/\">the university's website</a>, it is the oldest Catholic and Jesuit institution of higher learning in the United States. Classes began in 1792 and within the first year of the school's operations, the class size had grown to more than 40 students.</p>\n\tFLORIDA: Florida State University in Tallahassee\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6bacaac4049200115cb3ee?format=jpeg\" alt=\"florida state university\" height=\"667\" width=\"889\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Florida State University.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Fotoluminate LLC/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Florida State University in Tallahassee dates back to 1851. Though the <a href=\"https://www.rollins.edu/about-rollins/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\">first recognized college in the US is Rollings College</a> in Winter Park, Florida, Rollings wasn't founded until 1855, making Florida State University technically the oldest in the state.</p>\n\tGEORGIA: The University of Georgia in Athens\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6bad4ce3e76700117162e8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"University of Georgia\" height=\"666\" width=\"889\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The University of Georgia.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Bryan Pollard/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><a href=\"https://www.uga.edu/history.php#:~:text=When%20the%20University%20of%20Georgia,college%20or%20seminary%20of%20learning.\">The University of Georgia in Athens</a> became the first university in the country to have a state-supported charter in 1785. The university was established in 1801 after a group of board trustees officially selected a land site.</p>\n\tHAWAII: The University of Hawaii at Manoa in Honolulu\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6badd0e3e76700117162ef?format=jpeg\" alt=\"University Hawaii Manoa\" height=\"1568\" width=\"2099\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The University of Hawaii at Manoa.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Bill Morson/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The University of Hawaii at Manoa in Honolulu, Hawaii, was founded slightly more recently as far as old colleges go. According to <a href=\"https://manoa.hawaii.edu/about/history/\">the university's website</a>, it was founded in 1907 under the Morrill Act as \"a land-grant college of agriculture and mechanic arts.\"</p>\n\tIDAHO: Brigham Young University Idaho in Rexburg\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6baeaae3e76700117162f8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Brigham Young University Idaho\" height=\"1416\" width=\"1888\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Brigham Young University Idaho.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Danamallard51/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Brigham Young University Idaho in Rexburg, Idaho, was founded in 1888. It started as Bannock Stake Academy and is owned by the Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints. According to <a href=\"https://www2.byui.edu/PR/General/BYUIHistory2.htm\">the school's website</a>, the institution officially became known as Brigham Young University-Idaho in August 2001.</p>\n\tILLINOIS: McKendree University in Lebanon\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6bb03ec4049200115cb413?format=jpeg\" alt=\"McKendree University\" height=\"2227\" width=\"2969\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>McKendree University.\n<p class=\"copyright\">RozenskiP/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>McKendree University in Lebanon, Illinois, was founded in 1828 by pioneer methodists in the state. According to <a href=\"https://www.mckendree.edu/about/about-mck/history/index.php\">the university's website</a>, it is the oldest college in Illinois and the oldest in the nation with continuous ties to the United Methodist Church.</p>\n\tINDIANA: Vincennes University in Vincennes\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f736ebb0ab50d00184ad0bf?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Vincennes University\" height=\"820\" width=\"1094\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Vincennes University.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Google Maps</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Vincennes University in Vincennes, Indiana, opened in 1801 under the name Jefferson Academy. According to <a href=\"https://www.vinu.edu/hometown\">the university's website</a>, Vincennes is also the oldest city in Indiana, with many pieces of architecture dating back to its time as a French fur trading post.</p>\n\tIOWA: Loras College in Dubuque\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6bb222c4049200115cb423?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Loras College iowa\" height=\"683\" width=\"910\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Loras College.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Joe Raedle/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Loras College in Dubuque, Iowa, was founded in 1839 as a school intended to educate young men for the priesthood. <a href=\"https://www.loras.edu/about/history/\">Loras College adopted its present name in 1939</a>&#160;and became a coeducational institution in the fall of 1971.</p>\n\tKANSAS: Baker University in Baldwin City\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6bb4b9e3e767001171631e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Baker University\" height=\"2008\" width=\"2678\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Baker University.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mark Reinstein/Corbis/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Baker University in Baldwin City, Kansas, was founded in February 1858. The university opened its doors to students later that year.</p>\n\tKENTUCKY: Transylvania University in Lexington\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6bb536e3e7670011716322?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Transylvania university\" height=\"667\" width=\"889\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Transylvania University.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Julen Prieto/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Transylvania University in Lexington, Kentucky, was founded in 1780. <a href=\"https://www.transy.edu/about/transylvania/our-history/\">According to the university</a>, the first classes were held near Danville, Kentucky, in a cabin owned by one the first chairman of the Board of Trustees in 1785.</p>\n\tLOUISIANA: Centenary College of Louisiana in Shreveport\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6bb570e3e7670011716324?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Centenary College of Louisiana\" height=\"667\" width=\"889\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Centenary College of Louisiana.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mccallk69/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Centenary College of Louisiana in Shreveport was founded in 1825, during which time it was known as the College of Louisiana. It is the 43rd oldest college in the United States. According to <a href=\"https://www.centenary.edu/about/our-history/\">the university's website</a>, tuition in the early days of the school was just $50 per year, and room, board, and firewood were $7 per month.</p>\n\tMAINE: Bowdoin College in Brunswick\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6bb5b2e3e7670011716327?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Bowdoin College\" height=\"666\" width=\"888\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Bowdoin College.\n<p class=\"copyright\">EQRoy/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Bowdoin College in Brunswick, Maine, was established in 1794. According to <a href=\"https://www.britannica.com/topic/Bowdoin-College#:~:text=Maine's%20oldest%20college%2C%20Bowdoin%20was,Women%20were%20admitted%20in%201971.\">Britannica</a>, classes officially began in 1802, and women were admitted for the first time in 1971.</p>\n\tMARYLAND: St. John's College in Annapolis\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6bb699e3e7670011716337?format=jpeg\" alt=\"St. John&#39;s College Annapolis\" height=\"2375\" width=\"3166\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>St. John&#39;s College.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mark Gail/The Washington Post/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>St. John's College in Annapolis was founded in 1696. According to <a href=\"https://www.sjc.edu/about/history\">the school's website</a>, it is the third oldest college in the United States, behind Harvard University and College of William and Mary. It was originally founded under the name The King William's School.</p>\n\tMASSACHUSETTS: Harvard University in Cambridge\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ace6f22146e7128008b45f0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Cambridge Massachusetts harvard campus best cities america\" height=\"799\" width=\"1066\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Harvard University.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jon Bilous/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Harvard University is the oldest college in the entire country &#8212; it dates back to 1636. The school was named after a young minister by the name of John Harvard, who, <a href=\"https://www.harvard.edu/about-harvard/harvard-glance/history\">according to the university</a>, left his library and half of his estate to the institution upon his death in 1638.</p>\n\tMICHIGAN: The University of Michigan in Ann Arbor\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6bb730c4049200115cb44e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"University of Michigan in Ann Arbor\" height=\"2988\" width=\"3984\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The University of Michigan.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Dieon Roger/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The University of Michigan was founded in 1817 as a preparatory school in Detroit. <a href=\"https://www.britannica.com/topic/University-of-Michigan\">According to Britannica</a>, the school moved to its present site in Ann Arbor in 1837.</p>\n\tMINNESOTA: University of Minnesota – Twin Cities in Minneapolis\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5b64c22504f16232008b49e9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"University of Minnesota\" height=\"1333\" width=\"1778\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>University of Minnesota – Twin Cities.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Ken Wolter/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The University of Minnesota &#8211; Twin Cities was established in 1851, <a href=\"https://www.britannica.com/topic/University-of-Minnesota\">seven years before the creation of the state itself in 1858</a>. Both male and female students received instruction from the school before the school closed during the Civil War. The University of Minnesota reopened in 1867 and was reorganized as a university in 1869.</p>\n\tMISSISSIPPI: Mississippi College in Clinton\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5bb5378eac0a633aa50d3bd3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"mississippi college\" height=\"683\" width=\"911\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Mississippi College.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.yelp.com/biz_photos/mississippi-college-clinton-2?select=7cN-h3zpysRNFqYBlFDViA\" target=\"_blank\">Wikimedia Commons/Mississippi College</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><a href=\"https://www.mc.edu/about/history/early-years\">Founded in 1826 as Hampstead Academy</a>, Mississippi College is the oldest educational institution in Mississippi. It is located in Clinton, Mississippi, and was renamed Mississippi Academy in January 1827, when the school began offering classes to both male and female students.</p>\n\tMISSOURI: Saint Louis University in St. Louis\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6bb9a7e3e7670011716352?format=jpeg\" alt=\"st louis university\" height=\"657\" width=\"875\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Saint Louis University.\n<p class=\"copyright\">4kclips/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Saint Louis University was founded inside a private residence near the Mississippi River at the request of the Rev. Louis William DuBourg, Catholic Bishop of Louisiana, in 1818. Not only is Saint Louis University the oldest educational institution of higher learning in Missouri, but it's also the oldest institution west of the Mississippi River, <a href=\"https://www.slu.edu/timeline/index.php\">according to the school's website</a>.</p>\n\tMONTANA: Rocky Mountain College in Billings\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f73aee474fe5b0018a8e1ff?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Rocky Mountain College\" height=\"2674\" width=\"3568\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Rocky Mountain College.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Rocky Mountain College</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><a href=\"https://www.rocky.edu/about-rmc/history-traditions#:~:text=The%20story%20of%20Rocky%20Mountain,opened%20its%20doors%20in%20Helena.\">Rocky Mountain College</a> in Billings, Montana, dates back to 1878 and originally comprised of three separate colleges. In 1947, the schools combined to become Billings Polytechnic Institute, later named Rocky Mountain College.</p>\n\tNEBRASKA: Peru State College in Peru\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6bbb69e3e767001171635b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Peru State College\" height=\"667\" width=\"889\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Peru State College.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.yelp.com/biz/peru-state-college-peru\" target=\"_blank\">Peru State College/Yelp</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><a href=\"https://www.peru.edu/about#:~:text=Peru%20State%20College's%20History&#38;text=Nebraska's%20first%20college%2C%20established%20in,programs%20to%20around%202%2C400%20students.\">Peru State College</a> is the oldest college in Nebraska &#8212; it was founded in 1867. It was originally established as a teacher training school with 60 students attending classes in one building. However, the institution has since expanded immensely.</p>\n\tNEVADA: The University of Nevada in Reno\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6bbbabe3e767001171635e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"University of Nevada – Reno\" height=\"667\" width=\"889\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The University of Nevada.\n<p class=\"copyright\">f.christian/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><a href=\"https://www.unr.edu/about/history\">The University of Nevada</a> was founded in 1874 after the Morrill Land Grant Act of 1862. The University's first iteration was located in Elko but has since moved to Reno, Nevada.</p>\n\tNEW HAMPSHIRE: Dartmouth College in Hanover\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6bbc3ae3e7670011716362?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Dartmouth College\" height=\"667\" width=\"889\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Dartmouth College.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jay Yuan/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Dartmouth College was founded in 1769. It's the ninth-oldest university in the nation, <a href=\"https://home.dartmouth.edu/life-community/explore-green/history-traditions\">according to the school</a>, and has been in operation for more than 250 years.</p>\n\tNEW JERSEY: Princeton University in Princeton\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6df614c4049200115cb97f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Princeton University\" height=\"3337\" width=\"4449\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Princeton University.\n<p class=\"copyright\">John Greim / Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Princeton University was chartered in 1746, according to <a href=\"https://www.visitprinceton.org/princeton-university/history/#:~:text=Chartered%20in%201746%2C%20and%20known,was%20officially%20renamed%20Princeton%20University.\">the university's website</a>. The university was relocated to Princeton University in 1756 and changed its name from the College of New Jersey to Princeton University in 1896. Princeton is the fourth-oldest college in the United States.</p>\n\tNEW MEXICO: New Mexico State University in Las Cruces\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5bb53bbcac0a633acd207c56?format=jpeg\" alt=\"new mexico state university\" height=\"1398\" width=\"1864\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>New Mexico State University.\n<p class=\"copyright\">NMSU</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>New Mexico State University in Las Cruces, New Mexico, <a href=\"https://catalogs.nmsu.edu/nmsu/history-university/\">was founded in 1888 as the state's first land-grant university</a>. Throughout its history, the university has operated under multiple names, including Las Cruces College and New Mexico College of Agriculture and Mechanic Arts.&#160;</p>\n\tNEW YORK: Columbia University in New York\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6df63bc4049200115cb984?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Columbia University\" height=\"4000\" width=\"5333\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Columbia University.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Rob Kim/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Columbia University is the oldest college in the state of New York. It was founded in 1754 as King's College by royal charter of King George II of England, according to <a href=\"https://www.columbia.edu/content/history#:~:text=Columbia%20University%20was%20founded%20in,oldest%20in%20the%20United%20States.\">the school's website</a>.</p><p>It is the fifth oldest institute of higher learning in the United States and played a vital role in American history through some of its first students and trustees, namely \"John Jay, the first chief justice of the United States; Alexander Hamilton, the first secretary of the treasury; Gouverneur Morris, the author of the final draft of the U.S. Constitution; and Robert R. Livingston, a member of the five-man committee that drafted the Declaration of Independence,\" according to <a href=\"https://www.columbia.edu/content/history#:~:text=Columbia%20University%20was%20founded%20in,oldest%20in%20the%20United%20States.\">the school's website</a>.</p>\n\tNORTH CAROLINA: Salem College in Winston-Salem\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6df746c4049200115cb989?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Salem College\" height=\"667\" width=\"889\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Salem College.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Zhong Chen/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Salem College was founded in 1772, four years before the United States declared its independence from Great Britain. It was originally founded as a school for girls and is still recognized as the oldest educational institution for girls and women in America, according to <a href=\"https://www.salem.edu/abou\">the college's website</a>.</p>\n\tNORTH DAKOTA: The University of North Dakota in Grand Forks\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5b64b4ba1982d822008b4a67?format=jpeg\" alt=\"university of north dakota\" height=\"1500\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The University of North Dakota.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jacob Boomsma/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The University of North Dakota was founded in 1883, six years before North Dakota became recognized as a state. The very first graduating class was coeducational and consisted of six women and two men. Of them, Dr. Cora Smith King became the first woman to receive a medical license in the state of North Dakota, according to <a href=\"https://und.edu/about/history.html\">the university's website</a>.</p>\n\tOHIO: Ohio University in Athens\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6df7a1c4049200115cb991?format=jpeg\" alt=\"ohio university\" height=\"2391\" width=\"3189\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Ohio University.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Wendy van Overstreet/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Ohio University in Athens, Ohio, was founded in 1804 after the Ohio legislature approved a new act allowing the university to be established. Ohio University first offered classes in 1809, during which time the institution operated more like a high school than a college, according to <a href=\"http://ohiohistorycentral.org/w/Ohio_University\">the university's website</a>.</p><p>In 1822, after Ohio University was able to hire a team of higher-skilled faculty members, the school began to offer a traditional college program.</p>\n\tOKLAHOMA: University of Central Oklahoma in Edmond\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6e14080f4d550011032542?format=jpeg\" alt=\"univerversity of central oklahoma\" height=\"730\" width=\"973\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The University of Central Oklahoma.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.yelp.com/biz_photos/university-of-central-oklahoma-edmond-4?select=J3n9RJUW_hEFuezii0etnA\" target=\"_blank\">Shay B./Yelp</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The University of Central Oklahoma was founded in 1890. In November 1891, the very first class of 23 students met in the Epworth League Room inside the unfurnished First Methodist Church, according to <a href=\"https://www.uco.edu/history\">the school's website</a>.</p>\n\tOREGON: Willamette University in Salem\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6e1687259a51001905f3e6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Willamette University\" height=\"2310\" width=\"3081\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Willamette University.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Bob Pool/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Willamette University was established in 1842 as a missionary school. The university is one of the oldest coeducational colleges in the United States &#8212; the very first graduate of the university was a woman, and women were attending the School of Medicine as early as 1877, according to <a href=\"https://willamette.edu/about/history/index.html\">the Willamette University website</a>.</p>\n\tPENNSYLVANIA: The University of Pennsylvania in Philadelphia\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5b64c459959f34222e8b4839?format=jpeg\" alt=\"university of pennsylvania\" height=\"1332\" width=\"1776\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The University of Pennsylvania.\n<p class=\"copyright\">f11photo/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The University of Pennsylvania in Philadelphia dates back to 1740 when it was established as a charity school that would also house a place of worship for local people in Pennsylvania. It was the first American institute of higher learning to officially bear the name \"university,\" <a href=\"https://www.upenn.edu/about/history\">according to the school</a>.</p>\n\tRHODE ISLAND: Brown University in Providence\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6e16c40f4d550011032550?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Brown University\" height=\"1400\" width=\"1866\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Brown University.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Lane Turner/The Boston Globe via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Brown University was founded in 1764 as the third college in New England and the seventh in America. Originally located in Warren, Rhode Island, it was the first Ivy League school to accept students from all religious affiliations, according to <a href=\"https://250.brown.edu/browns-history.html\">the school's website</a>.</p>\n\tSOUTH CAROLINA: College of Charleston in Charleston\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6e172a0f4d550011032553?format=jpeg\" alt=\"College of Charleston\" height=\"2663\" width=\"3551\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>College of Charleston.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Grindstone Media Group/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The College of Charleston was founded in 1770 and officially charted in 1785, according to <a href=\"https://www.britannica.com/topic/College-of-Charleston\">Britannica</a>. The city of Charleston took control of the college in 1836, making it the first municipal college in the nation.</p>\n\tSOUTH DAKOTA: Augustana University in Sioux Falls\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3c0c46650894001d072258?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Augustana University\" height=\"3024\" width=\"4032\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Augustana University.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Michael R Helland/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Augustana University in Sioux Falls, South Dakota, was founded in 1860, though the university's roots were established as Hillsboro Academy, which was founded in 1835. The <a href=\"http://www.augie.edu/about-augustana/history-augustana-university\">first class was held on September 1, 1860</a>, which coincides with the founding date of Augustana's sister-college, Augustana College, in Rock Island, Illinois.</p>\n\tTENNESSEE: Tusculum College in Tusculum\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6e17db0f4d55001103255a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Tusculum College\" height=\"703\" width=\"938\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tusculum College.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.yelp.com/biz_photos/tusculum-college-greeneville-3?select=ztl2wmjI_0Aw8mSs6tYh8Q\" target=\"_blank\">Rob B./Yelp</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Tusculum College in Tusculum, Tennessee, was chartered in 1794 as Greeneville College. In 1844, the renamed Tusculum Academy officially adopted the name Tusculum College, according to <a href=\"https://tuproud.tusculum.edu/about-us/\">the school's website</a>.</p>\n\tTEXAS: Southwestern University in Georgetown\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5bbb601076545305901ca756?format=jpeg\" alt=\"southwestern college\" height=\"720\" width=\"960\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Southwestern University.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Southwestern College</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Southwestern University in Georgetown was founded in 1840, five years after Colonel William B. Travis wrote a letter to the New York Christian Advocate asking for a Methodist presence to be established in Texas, according to <a href=\"https://www.southwestern.edu/about-southwestern/our-history/\">the school's website</a>.</p><p>The school <a href=\"https://www.southwestern.edu/about-southwestern/our-history/\">claims to have been the site of many firsts</a>, including the first homecoming on record and the first student literary journal in the state.</p>\n\tUTAH: The University of Utah in Salt Lake City\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5b645d16e361c074048b45c5?format=jpeg\" alt=\"university of utah\" height=\"1334\" width=\"1778\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The University of Utah.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jason Finn/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Originally named the University of Deseret, the University of Utah in Salt Lake City, Utah, was founded in 1850. <a href=\"https://www.uen.org/utah_history_encyclopedia/u/UNIVERSITY_OF_UTAH.shtml\">The first term began in November 1850</a>, during which time only male students were admitted. At the start of the second term, both men and women were allowed to attend.</p>\n\tVERMONT: Castleton University in Castleton\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6e375da5fb5800198b2f35?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Castleton University\" height=\"2660\" width=\"3546\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Castleton University.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Castleton University</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Nestled in the quaint town of Castleton, Vermont, Castleton University was founded in 1787. It is the <a href=\"https://www.castleton.edu/about-castleton/quick-facts/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\">18th oldest institute of higher learning in the country</a>, according to its website, and sits on a historic 165-acre campus.</p>\n\tVIRGINIA: College of William & Mary in Williamsburg\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6e19880f4d550011032574?format=jpeg\" alt=\"College of William &#38; Mary\" height=\"2688\" width=\"3583\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The College of William &#38; Mary.\n<p class=\"copyright\">aceshot1/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The College of William &#38; Mary is located in the historic colonial town of Williamsburg, Virginia, and dates all the way back to 1693. It is the second-oldest institute of higher learning in the US and has a lengthy list of esteemed and influential alumni members.</p><p>According to <a href=\"https://www.wm.edu/offices/deanofstudents/services/communityvalues/studenthandbook/history_of_william_and_mary/index.php#:~:text=Founded%20in%201693%20by%20the,still%20in%20use%20in%20America.\">the school's website</a>, American presidents Thomas Jefferson, James Monroe, and John Tyler all studied at William &#38; Mary, in addition to 16 members of the Continental Congress and four signers of the Declaration of Independence.&#160;</p>\n\tWASHINGTON: The University of Washington in Seattle\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6e19d40f4d550011032579?format=jpeg\" alt=\"University of Washington\" height=\"2000\" width=\"2668\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The University of Washington.\n<p class=\"copyright\">f11photo/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The University of Washington in Seattle, originally named&#160;the Territorial University of Washington, is the oldest in the state &#8212; it was founded in 1861. In 1867, the <a href=\"https://myuvn.com/a-brief-history-of-the-university-of-washington/\">tuition price to attend UW was just $30</a>.&#160;</p>\n\tWEST VIRGINIA: Bethany College in Bethany\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6e36dd1fbb1b0019638b0c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Bethany College\" height=\"2678\" width=\"3571\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Bethany College.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Bethany College</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Bethany College was founded in 1840, though the town of Bethany dates back to 1769. By the time that West Virginia was recognized as a US state in 1863, <a href=\"https://www.bethanywv.edu/about-bethany/historic-bethany/\">Bethany College was the only institute of higher learning in the state</a> to offer collegiate degrees.</p>\n\tWISCONSIN: Carroll University in Waukesha\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f736cb974fe5b0018a8e00c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Carroll University\" height=\"951\" width=\"1268\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Carroll University.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Carroll University</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Carroll University was chartered in 1846 by the Wisconsin Territorial Legislature, two years before Wisconsin became a state. The school was originally established as an academy in 1841 by settlers living in the Wisconsin Territory community of Prairieville. When the college first opened, the enrollment consisted of five students and two faculty members, Eleazar Root and John W. Sterling, according to <a href=\"https://www.carrollu.edu/about/history-timeline\">the university's website</a>.</p>\n\tWYOMING: The University of Wyoming in Laramie\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6e1c19259a51001905f415?format=jpeg\" alt=\"University of Wyoming\" height=\"1725\" width=\"2301\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The University of Wyoming.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jillian Cain Photography/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The University of Wyoming in Laramie, Wyoming, was founded as a land-grant university in 1886. When the school first opened, there were <a href=\"https://visitlaramie.org/the-historic-campus-of-the-university-of-wyoming-brochure\">five faculty members and 42 students</a>.</p><ul class=\"read-more-links\"><li>Read more:</li><li><a href=\"https://www.insider.com/oldest-city-us-states-2018-3\" data-read-more-link=\"\" data-e2e-name=\"read-more-link\">The oldest town in every state</a></li><li><a href=\"https://www.insider.com/oldest-building-us-states-2018-4\" data-read-more-link=\"\" data-e2e-name=\"read-more-link\">The oldest building in every state</a></li><li><a href=\"https://www.insider.com/oldest-restaurant-in-every-state-2017-9\" data-read-more-link=\"\" data-e2e-name=\"read-more-link\">The oldest restaurant in every state</a></li></ul>\n</div><div src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f84946fc255d800190b9587?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Chipotle TikTok menu hacks 25\" height=\"1666\" width=\"2222\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Chipotle is now charging for a side tortilla.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Irene Jiang/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Chipotle is now charging $0.25 for a side tortilla.</li>\n<li>The free tortilla hack has historically been one of customers' favorite ways to get free food from the chain.&#160;</li>\n<li>Chipotle has been able to monitor ingredient costs and portion control more closely during the pandemic, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/chipotles-digital-order-boom-reveals-flaw-in-assembly-line-system-2020-9\">as more people order online and via app.&#160;</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The era of the free Chipotle tortilla has come to an end.&#160;</p><p>Last week, the chain announced internally that it will no longer offer free side tortillas. As of Monday, customers will be charged $0.25 for every side tortilla added to their orders.&#160;</p><p>Chipotle did not respond to Business Insider's request for comment on the change. The chain's app displayed a $0.25 charge for a side tortilla as of Monday morning.&#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f8d922fc21cfb0019468b39?format=jpeg\" alt=\"chipotle\" height=\"413\" width=\"828\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tortillas are no longer free at Chipotle.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kate Taylor/Chipotle app</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The free side tortilla has long been one of customers' favorite ways to get free food at the chain. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-get-big-portions-at-chipotle-2014-11\">Typically,</a> a burrito bowl packs in more ingredients than a burrito — meaning a bowl plus a free tortilla yields more food overall.&#160;</p><p>Chipotle has been able to gather more data about its ingredient costs during the pandemic, as more people are ordering ahead via app or the chain's website.</p><p>Chief financial officer Jack Hartung <a href=\"https://seekingalpha.com/article/4375001-chipotle-mexican-grill-inc-cmg-ceo-brian-niccol-presents-raymond-james-north-american?part=single\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"bf58b4c8bb52debc566372f02acebf86\">said</a> in September that employees have been more precise in their portion control when they are preparing food ahead of time for customers. When ordering digitally, the only way for customers to receive more than the standard size is to ask — and pay — for extra.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/chipotles-digital-order-boom-reveals-flaw-in-assembly-line-system-2020-9\">The pandemic revealed a huge flaw in Chipotle's restaurant assembly-line system</a></em></p><p>\"We're not restricting what the customer is allowed to do, either in terms of portion or in terms of adding additional ingredients,\" Hartung said at the Raymond James North American Equities Conference. \"But our portion sizes are much more consistent because there's not somebody pointing at every single pan ... the crew will see just the way that a customer is looking at them and think, 'Oh, I better put another scoop in.'\"</p><p>\"We're finding things like that are resulting in better controls at the food line,\" Hartung added. \"We do think, certainly, because digital will be more sticky, a lot of that will stay. But we also think it's an opportunity for us to get better execution on the front line as well as people ordering in restaurant.\"&#160;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a launched an MTV-style, livestreaming channel on Monday that features exclusive music videos and interviews</li>\n<li>The service can be found on the Apple Music and TV apps and is free for users in the US.</li>\n<li>The channel represents the tech giant's first foray into music videos.</li>\n<li>MTV popularized the music video channel concept in the 1980s, long before YouTube and Vevo became the go-to places to view them.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Apple is launching a 24-hour music video station that will be free for users in the US.</p><p><a href=\"http://apple.co/AppleMusicTV\">Apple Music TV</a> will feature exclusives including new music videos and premieres, live shows, and events. It will also feature chart countdowns and guests, the company told Business Insider in an email. The station launched Monday with a \"special\" countdown of the top 100 most-streamed songs ever on Apple Music and plans to release new music videos every Friday.</p><p>On Thursday, the station will be playing music blocks of Bruce Springsteen's greatest videos in an all-day takeover ahead of his upcoming release \"Letter to You.\" An exclusive interview with Springsteen and Apple Music 1 radio host and DJ Zane Lowe will also air on Thursday, signaling potential ties between Apple's new station and the company's existing music programming as <a href=\"https://variety.com/2020/music/news/apple-music-tv-launch-videos-1234809088/\">Variety</a> notes.</p><p>On Friday, Apple's channel will release two exclusive new music videos by the artist Joji and their song \"777\" and SAINt JHN's \"Gorgeous,\" according to the company.</p><p>The service can be found under a tab on the Apple Music and Apple TV apps. The tagline reads \"the music will be televised. Watch now for free.\"</p><p>The launch of the service represents Apple's first foray into music videos, an arena that has largely been dominated by YouTube in the past decade as more and more artists and listeners turned online. Before YouTube hit the scene, it was the likes of MTV in the 1980s and 1990s, and later VH1, that popularized how people could watch music videos.&#160;</p><p>Apple Music TV is yet another move by the company to set itself apart in the audio and video streaming landscapes. Apple unveiled its \"Planet of the Apes\" TV series in early 2017 as it was first rolling out its TV programs. And in late 2019, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/apple-tv-plus-streaming-service-price-launch-date-2019-9\">Apple launched TV Plus</a>, a streaming service that put the company in the same ballgame as competitors like Netflix and Hulu.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a election result,\" a Goldman team led by chief economist Jan Hatzius wrote on Monday. \"Fiscal policy differences between Republicans and Democrats in the Senate are greater than differences between the presidential candidates.\"&#160;</p><p>A Democratic majority in Congress would result in \"substantially more fiscal support,\" and the chief economist said multiple polls and statistical models more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Mark Zuckerberg signed off on a Facebook algorithm change in 2017 that throttled traffic to progressive news sites, costing journalism outlet Mother Jones hundreds of thousands of dollars, according to <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/how-mark-zuckerberg-learned-politics-11602853200\">a report by The Wall Street Journal</a> and <a href=\"https://twitter.com/ClaraJeffery/status/1317199501136859136\">comments by Mother Jones senior staff</a> published Friday.</p><p>The Wall Street Journal report cited sources that said Facebook was concerned about negatively affecting conservative news outlets when it planned on changing the algorithm that governs users' news feeds in 2017. In turn, Mark Zuckerberg signed off on an alternative that targeted \"left-leaning sites like Mother Jones...more than previously planned,\" WSJ reported.</p><p>Following Friday's report, Mother Jones editor in chief Clara Jeffrey slammed the social media company, estimating that the move cost the publication $400,000 to $600,000. In addition, Jeffrey, and Mother Jones editorial director Ben Dreyfuss, wrote that Facebook representatives had lied to them in meetings about the change in 2017. Dreyfuss tweeted that, \"they just swore up and down that wasn't what was happening,\" on Friday.</p><p>\"We did not make changes with the intent of impacting individual publishers,\" a Facebook spokesperson wrote in a statement to Business Insider on Friday. \"We only made updates after they were reviewed by many different teams across many disciplines to ensure the rationale was clear and consistent and could be explained to all publishers.\"</p><p>In 2019, Mother Jones <a href=\"https://www.motherjones.com/politics/2019/02/how-facebook-screwed-us-all/\">published a report</a> that claimed Facebook was \"killing real news.\" It used its own traffic data to show how after Facebook-referred traffic surpassed 20 million page views in early 2017, traffic diminished to less than 5 million page views in late 2017 and 2018.&#160;</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Person Woman Man Camera TV  (@ClaraJeffery) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1317191624653369344?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">October 16, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>&#160;</p><p>These dates align with the Wall Street Journal's report that Facebook made changes to the algorithm that de-emphasized Mother Jones' content in late 2017.</p><p>When she published the 2019 report, Jeffrey wasn't aware that Facebook had made any policy changes \"targeting us in particular,\" she tweeted on Friday. Jeffrey called Facebook's actions, \"an intentional change to hurt shops that do serious investigative journalism,\" in a tweet on Friday.</p><p>Read The Wall Street Journal's full report <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/how-mark-zuckerberg-learned-politics-11602853200\">here</a>. Read Jeffrey's full comments <a href=\"https://twitter.com/ClaraJeffery/status/1317199501136859136\">here</a>.&#160;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/kuhvOmOPqZk\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 19 Oct 2020 14:26:55 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5f8a23819e9fe40019009e9c?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"0656ec8f6aa730d41a156e4b1efeae7f","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn71@2020_2/2020/10/19/15-59-39-110_fd242b554074b4a9.webp","destWidth":1552,"destHeight":1164,"sourceBytes":82832,"destBytes":82832,"author":"ijibilian@businessinsider.com (Isabella Jibilian)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f5fe2db57b7da001ee118b8?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn44@2020_4/2020/10/19/15-59-43-581_91f81a6f6b163fb9.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn56@2020_5/2020/10/19/15-59-47-418_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=kuhvOmOPqZk:PXgDQ5ALpVk:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn3@2020_6/2020/10/19/15-59-40-776_6418acf6a33f3e9a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=kuhvOmOPqZk:PXgDQ5ALpVk:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn28@2020_1/2020/10/19/15-59-48-708_24302e6bbdf22dbf.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn91@2020_5/2020/10/19/15-59-43-999_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=kuhvOmOPqZk:PXgDQ5ALpVk:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn35@2020_4/2020/10/19/15-59-43-675_b58da2aa245cc9bd.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/kuhvOmOPqZk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn59@2020_2/2020/10/19/15-59-44-649_afe2cd4e6f837b70.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1603123145993},{"createdTime":"2020-10-19 23:59:06","updatedTime":"2020-10-19 23:59:06","title":"A SPAC is a high-risk but potentially profitable way to get in on the ground floor of a new stock — here's everything investors need to know","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-a-spac","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f8a13f99e9fe40019009e84?format=jpeg\" alt=\"richard branson virgin galactic ipo spac\" height=\"1249\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Sir Richard Branson on the floor of the New York Stock Exchange as their SPAC-sponsored Virgin Galactic begins  public trading in October 2019.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Brendan McDermid/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>A Special Purpose Acquisition Company (SPAC) is a company created solely to merge or acquire another business and take it public &#8212; a cheaper, faster alternative to an initial public offering (IPO).</li>\n<li>Investors essentially write blank checks to SPACs, which can take up to two years to target and buy another firm.</li>\n<li>SPACs offer individual investors the chance to get in on the ground floor of a potentially big stock, but are also highly risky.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/investing-reference\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\"><strong>Visit Insider's Investing Reference library for more stories</strong></a><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\"><strong>.</strong></a></li>\n</ul><ul class=\"read-more-links\"><li><p>A lot of individuals would love to get in early on an initial public offering (IPO) — a company's launch on the stock exchange — before the shares start jumping on fever-pitch demand. But pension funds and professionals usually get there first, leaving \"retail investors,\" as Wall Street calls them, typically picking up the post-offering breadcrumbs — and often paying a higher price.</p><p>But a back-door, formerly out-of-favor IPO approach known as a SPAC has recently roared back in popularity among entrepreneurs and venture capitalists. It may offer a new opportunity for small investors to get in on the action at the beginning.</p><h2>What is a SPAC?</h2><p>SPAC is an acronym for a Special Purpose Acquisition Company, basically a publicly traded firm that has no operations, no assets — other than a war chest of cash — and just one stated business plan: to eventually buy another company.</p><p>A SPAC is generally formed by a group of investors, called sponsors, with a strong background in a particular industry or business sector. They raise funds from other investors, and use the money to acquire an existing, privately held company — and then take it public in an IPO.</p><p>When they launch the SPAC, the sponsors generally either don't have a specific target in mind, or they're not ready to name it in order to avoid the extensive paperwork and disclosures required by the Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC).</p><p>The early-bird underwriters and institutional investors, and the individual investors who generally come in later, typically have no idea exactly how the sponsors will spend the money. So early investors are basically relying on the sponsors' reputation in the hope of snagging a good investment.</p><p>But they've got to be prepared to wait. Even after a SPAC goes public, it can take up to two years to pick and announce the target company it wants to acquire, or technically speaking, merge with (the corporate charter specifies the exact time frame, per SEC regulations). If it doesn't, the SPAC is liquidated, and funds it's raised are supposed to be returned to investors.</p><p>All this uncertainty is one reason why most SPACs trade at only $10 a share. Of course, the assumption is that when, and if, they acquire a company and take it public, the share prices will soar. At this point, investors can cash out, or hold on for longer-term gains.</p><h2>How SPACs work&#160;</h2><p>If the SPAC set-up sounds like a situation ripe for abuse — it once was. Back in the 1980s, a lot of fraud surrounded these blank check companies, as they were then known. Many were purely shell companies, offering thinly traded<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-are-penny-stocks\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> penny stocks</a> or \"pink sheets.\" Often these firms either absconded with investors' cash or engaged in overvalued insider deals that left many investors with a bagful of nothing.</p><p>Since then, however, the metamorphosis from blank check company to SPAC has involved more than just a name change. The SEC has tightened regulations and procedures for these ventures.</p><p>Now, for example, a SPAC generally has to place the investor money in a trust or escrow account to keep it secure until the target company is publicly announced. At that point, if investors don't like the looks of the deal, they should be able to recover their funds.</p><p>SPACs also have to register with the SEC, even if they're relatively small (which in the IPO universe means assets under $1 million).</p></li></ul><div class=\"insider-raw-embed\"><iframe title=\"SPACs are soaring in numbers and size\" aria-label=\"Grouped Bars\" id=\"datawrapper-chart-SDcem\" src=\"https://datawrapper.dwcdn.net/SDcem/4/\" scrolling=\"no\" frameborder=\"0\" style=\"width: 0; min-width: 100% ; border: none;\" height=\"630\"></iframe><script type=\"text/javascript\">!function(){\"use strict\";window.addEventListener(\"message\",(function(a){if(void 0!==a.data[\"datawrapper-height\"])for(var e in a.data[\"datawrapper-height\"]){var t=document.getElementById(\"datawrapper-chart-\"+e)||document.querySelector(\"iframe[src*='\"+e+\"']\");t&&(t.style.height=a.data[\"datawrapper-height\"][e]+\"px\")}}))}();</script></div><h2>SPAC Pros and Cons</h2><p>Like any investment, SPACs have advantages and disadvantages.</p><h3>Advantages of SPACs</h3><ul><li><strong>They're cheap</strong>. Many SPACs are priced at $10 a share, well within reach of retail investors. And they stay low for a while. \"SPAC IPOs on average don't jump on the first day of trading,\" notes Jay R. Ritter, the Joseph B. Cordell Eminent Scholar Chair at the University of Florida's Warrington College of Business, who researches IPOs. \"The average increase this year on the first day of trading has been 1.7%, so buying in the market might mean paying $10.17 or so.\"</li><li><strong>They invest in hot areas.</strong> The new breed of SPACs focuses on sexy sectors in the tech or consumer fields. Promising startups like <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/chamath-palihapitiya-spac-buys-opendoor-quiet-period-2020-9\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Opendoor</a>, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/clover-health-spac-plans-and-growth-projections-for-medicare-2020-10\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Clover Health</a>, and electric automaker Nikola are among the firms that have gone public via SPACs.</li><li><strong>They're open to individual investors</strong>. Even though institutional investors usually go to the front of the line for SPAC offerings, the high number of shares sold makes it easier for smaller investors to get a piece of the action.<strong style=\"color: #222222;\">&#160;</strong></li></ul><h3>Disadvantages of SPACs</h3><ul><li><strong>Blind investment.</strong> SPAC investors usually don't know how their money will be used — what the SPAC's target company is (often the sponsors don't know either). So the deal's impossible to evaluate.</li><li><strong>Lag time.</strong> There can be a long lag between the time investors pump money into a SPAC and when it actually buys up a company and starts operations. Your money may sit for up to two years in an escrow account. If no acquisition happens, your funds are returned, but idling capital for that long may be painful.</li><li><strong>Mixed track record</strong>. In a July 2020 report, Goldman Sachs analyzed the performance of 56 SPACs — primarily in the technology, industrials, energy, and financial segments, — that \"merged\" with their target companies beginning in January 2018. \"During the one-month and three-month periods following the acquisition announcement, the average SPAC outperformed the S&#38;P 500 by 1 percentage point (pp) and 11 pp, respectively, and beat the Russell 2000 by 6 pp and 15 pp, respectively,\" the report notes. \"However, the average SPAC underperformed both indexes during the 3, 6, and 12-months after the merger completion.\"</li></ul><p>Of course, some SPACs do better than that. For example, <strong>Virgin Galactic Holdings </strong>(<a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/spce-stock\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">SPCE</a>) — a particularly high-profile offering — has appreciated 146% in the year since it went public via a SPAC in October 2019.&#160;</p><h2>Why SPACS are becoming popular</h2><p>SPACs embarked on their newly respectable road in the mid-2010s. Big-name entrepreneurs, hedge-fund managers, and celebrities like Richard Branson, Bill Ackerman, and Michael Jordan became involved in them, as did mutual fund companies like Fidelity and T. Rowe Price, and investment banks like Morgan Stanley, Credit Suisse, and Goldman Sachs.</p><p>Their numbers swelled in 2020. As of early October 2020, SPACs have launched 128 IPOs, raising a total of $49.1 billion, according to SPAC Research, which gathers data on SPACs. That's up from 2019 when just 59 SPACs raised a total of $13.6 billion.</p><p>Certainly, the COVID-19 pandemic has been a factor. SPACs tend to<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/spac-blank-check-companies-explained-2020-5\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> fare better in periods of stock market decline</a> because of the way they work.&#160;</p><p>Also, compared to a traditional IPO, SPACs offer certain advantages to sponsor-organizers and to the companies who want to go public. One is the streamlined disclosure requirements that save time, money, and trees.</p><p>SPAC IPOs are further turbocharged because there are fewer people involved. A traditional IPO involves \"multiple investors negotiating with issuers and underwriters simultaneously, about specific terms like the offering price, executive compensation, underwriter rights, and multiple other issues,\" says Tyler Gellasch, executive director of Healthy Markets Association, a nonprofit, investor educational coalition. \"But in a SPAC, it's often just the sponsor and the target company at the table.\"</p><p>So deals can move faster.</p><h2>How to invest in SPACS</h2><p>Getting into a SPAC is not as simple as buying regular equities: Hedge funds, mutual funds, and other deep-pocketed institutional investors typically find out about a new SPAC first. \"It helps if a would-be investor has an existing relationship with a SPAC sponsor,\" says Tyler Gellasch.&#160;</p><p>But if Michael Jordan isn't among your contacts, there are other ways to break into the world of SPACs:</p><ul><li>Your friendly stockbroker or wealth manager. Ask them to keep an eye out for offerings</li><li>&#160;The websites of IPO-oriented investment banks. One SPAC specialist, <a href=\"https://www.earlybirdcapital.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Early Bird Capital</a>, lists companies that are actively seeking targets.</li><li>&#160;The NASDAQ website also lists upcoming IPOs, including SPACs, which can be identified by a ticker symbol that generally ends with a \"U.\"</li><li>&#160;Industry associations like SPAC Research sometimes highlight S-1 filings, which give formal notice of a SPAC's intention to go public.&#160;</li></ul><h2>The financial takeaway</h2><p>A SPAC is definitely not \"a 'widows and orphans' investment,\" according to Gellasch. \"For one thing, you may be tying up your money for a year or more without knowing what the ultimate investment will be. The sponsor and institutional investors may know — at least generally — what they're looking to do with the funds, but the small investor will likely be in the dark.\"</p><p>\"Until a deal is announced, the investor is just hoping that a good merger will happen,\" Ritter adds. And of course, there are no guarantees as to returns after it does. SPACs are speculative animals. They tend to acquire growth companies — start-ups and fledgling firms — which, by their nature, are higher-risk than, say, established <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-are-blue-chip-stocks\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">blue-chip</a> companies.</p><p>Still, SPACs offer smaller investors a way to get into the IPO game — if not up in front with the big players, at least not too far behind them.</p><h2>Related Coverage in&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/investing-reference\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\">Investing</a>:</h2><ul class=\"read-more-links\"><li><h3><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/top-spac-underwriters-law-firms-investors-blank-check-volume-fees-2020-9\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\">Meet 16 bankers, lawyers, and capital providers helping engineer a $40 billion blank-check craze that's fast-tracking companies to public markets</a></h3></li><li><h3><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/ipos-top-largest-initial-public-offerings-all-time-ranked-cash-2020-7-1029373999\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Here are the 11 largest IPOs of all time</a></h3></li><li><h3><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/spac-etf-first-blank-check-begins-trading-stock-market-nyse-2020-10-1029640817\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">First blank-check ETF begins trading as SPAC euphoria continues</a></h3></li><li><h3><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biggest-companies-to-go-public-through-a-spac-2020-10\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Going public through a SPAC isn't just for the unsexy startups anymore. charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Atlantic Sports Fitness, Krakow, pictured in 2011.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Google Streetview</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>A gym in Krakow, Poland, is trying to rebrand itself as a church in an attempt to get around new coronavirus restrictions.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/atlantickrakow\">In a Saturday Facebook post</a>, traffic-light system on Thursday to respond to record numbers of new cases in the country.&#160;</li>\n<li>Krakow is in the \"red zone,\" which requires gyms to close but churches to open with social distancing, according to the <a href=\"https://wyborcza.pl/7,82983,26401289,rzad-wprowadza-nowe-obostrzenia-i-rozszerza-czerwone-strefy.html\">Gazeta Wyborcza</a> newspaper.</li>\n<li>The gym's manager said people's jobs and health would be at risk if it shuts down.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>A gym in Krakow, Poland, is trying to rebrand itself as a \"Church of the Healthy Body\" in order to stay open during new coronavirus lockdown restrictions.</p><p>The manager of Atlantic Sports Fitness, Marta Jamróz, <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/atlantickrakow\">wrote in a Saturday Facebook post</a>: \"Since fitness classes cannot function ... a religious congregation of members are starting today at our club the 'Church of the Healthy Body.'\"</p><p>Jamróz also referred to the gym's trainers as \"the elder council.\"</p><p>The move came after Polish Prime Minister Mateusz Morawiecki announced on Thursday new national restrictions in a tiered \"traffic light\" system asking people to stay home, <a href=\"https://wyborcza.pl/7,82983,26401289,rzad-wprowadza-nowe-obostrzenia-i-rozszerza-czerwone-strefy.html\">according to Polish newspaper Gazeta Wyborcza</a>.</p><p>In the \"red zone\" — which includes Krakow — gyms and swimming pools must close, the paper reported.</p><p>The new rules came in response to a record leap in coronavirus cases in the country. New cases ballooned in Poland this fall, <a href=\"https://www.arcgis.com/apps/opsdashboard/index.html#/bda7594740fd40299423467b48e9ecf6\">according to Johns Hopkins University's tracker</a>, rising to just under 10,000 a day on Sunday. During the summer, daily new cases had never risen above 1,000.&#160;</p><p>But the new rules allow church gatherings in the red zone, as long as there is one person per 75 square feet, according to Gazeta Wyborcza.</p><p>The situation apparently prompted Atlantic Sports Fitness to rebrand.</p><p>\"Everything according to the law,\" Jamróz wrote. She did not describe the nature of the events, or how distanced customers would be.</p><p>She said that \"none of us wanted to believe it\" when the new restrictions were announced, expressing gym employees' concern for people's health and their own jobs if it closed. Jamróz said the gym follows \"all sanitary rules.\"</p><p>\"If someone doesn't want to come to the club, they don't have to!\" she wrote. \"So why do you close places where people care about the health and condition and follow all sanitary rules?! We are not only fighting for health! We are now fighting for survival! About our jobs!\"</p><p>Atlantic Sports Fitness did not immediately respond to Business Insider's request for comment on whether it has been allowed to reopen under the apparent rebrand.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f62580557b7da001ee1207b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Golds Gym coronavirus\" height=\"1867\" width=\"2400\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A Gold&#39;s Gym branch East Northport, New York, in August 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gettyimages.com/detail/news-photo/large-signs-about-sanitizing-are-posted-around-golds-gym-in-news-photo/1268062219?adppopup=true\" target=\"_blank\">J. Conrad Williams Jr./Newsday via Getty Images</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Gyms have been the site of coronavirus outbreaks through the pandemic, such as a <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/--spin-studio-in-canada-has-72-person-coronavirus-outbreak-despite-safety-measures-9402277\">Canadian spin studio that saw at least 72 people catch the virus</a> despite strong hygiene measures.</p><p>Infectious diseases expert Dr. Susan Hassig <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/riskiest-to-least-risky-activities-during-coronavirus-pandemic-ranked-2020-5?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">previously told Business Insider</a> that going to gyms is a \"medium- to high-risk\" activity.&#160;</p><p>The pandemic has been calamitious for the industry, causing several US fitness and sporting-goods companies to file for bankruptcy in 2020, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fitness-sporting-goods-retailers-filed-bankruptcy-liquidation-closing-stores-2020-9?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">according to Business Insider's Bethany Biron</a>.&#160;</p><p>Repeat lockdowns and closures have forced adaptations as diverse as holding virtual classes to holding sessions in bubbles, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/12-ways-pandemic-has-changed-fitness-as-we-know-it-2020-8?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">Biron also reported</a>. But this may be the first time a gym has rebranded as a church.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/poland-gym-rebrands-church-of-the-healthy-body-coronavirus-restrictions-2020-10'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a
