Jankowicz)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f8d7bb29e9fe4001900a015?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn47@2020_5/2020/10/19/15-59-48-220_f4f193c8551ad843.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f62580557b7da001ee1207b?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn11@2020_3/2020/10/19/15-59-49-346_5ab9b24d92867bce.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn56@2020_5/2020/10/19/15-59-47-418_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=9DTAH-FViDM:VCQriFPwL6k:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn39@2020_5/2020/10/19/15-59-48-163_dbf19d394ee9f615.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=9DTAH-FViDM:VCQriFPwL6k:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn64@2020_5/2020/10/19/15-59-40-428_d08dd974421dcbff.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn91@2020_5/2020/10/19/15-59-43-999_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=9DTAH-FViDM:VCQriFPwL6k:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn92@2020_4/2020/10/19/15-59-48-626_985e40b5d4e247f9.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/9DTAH-FViDM":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn20@2020_4/2020/10/19/15-59-47-931_10d3c40fd2e52a36.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1603123146006},{"createdTime":"2020-10-19 23:59:05","updatedTime":"2020-10-19 23:59:05","title":"Google's $100 Nest Audio is the new Google Assistant smart speaker to beat, but Amazon's upcoming Echo could offer better value for fans of Alexa","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/google-nest-audio-smart-speaker-review","description":"<p class=\"financial-disclaimer\"><i>When you buy through our links, we may earn money from our affiliate partners. <a href=\"https://www.insider-inc.com/commerce-on-insider-inc/\">Learn more.</a></i></p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f8d9360c21cfb0019468b3b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Google nest audio 1\" height=\"843\" width=\"1125\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Christian de Looper/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\"><li><a href=\"https://shop-links.co/1721072491310276872\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\"><strong>Google's Nest Audio</strong></a><strong> replaces the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/google-home-review-2016-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Google Home</a> as the company's flagship smart speaker.</strong></li><li><strong>The device features better sound quality than the previous model, and offers an updated design with multiple color options that should look good in any home.</strong></li><li><strong>With solid audio performance and a competitive $100 price tag, the </strong><a href=\"https://shop-links.co/1721072491310276872\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored\"><strong>Nest Audio</strong></a><strong> is the new go-to smart speaker for Google Assistant users.</strong></li><li><strong>That being said, Amazon's upcoming <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-echo-2020-specs-price-release-date#all-new-echo-1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">fourth-generation Echo</a> could potentially offer a better value for buyers open to using Alexa.&#160;</strong></li><li><strong>For more speaker recommendations, check out our roundup of <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/best-speaker-deals\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">the best speaker deals</a>.</strong></li></ul><div id=\"ProductCard_5f74e95ebe509c36a745efed\" style=\"position:relative; display:block; width: 100%\"><iframe src=\"https://produktor.businessinsider.com/productCardService?id=5f74e95ebe509c36a745efed&type=small&live=true\" width=\"100%\" height=\"150%\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"\" style=\"position:absolute; top:0; left: 0\"></iframe></div><p>The Google Home has long been one of <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/best-smart-speaker-amazon-echo\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">the best smart speakers</a> around, not necessarily because of its high-end audio, but because of how intelligent Google Assistant is. But, despite its smarts, the Home is also an aging product. First launched in 2016, the speaker can't help but feel a little stale in 2020.</p><p>With that in mind, there's finally a refresh, and it represents Google's renewed attempt to offer a better audio experience to go along with its already impressive digital assistant.</p><p>The <a href=\"https://shop-links.co/1721072491310276872\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow nofollow noopener sponsored sponsored nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Google Nest Audio</a> offers a totally different design compared to the Google Home. Perhaps most important is that under the hood the speaker now features a 75mm woofer and a 19mm tweeter, instead of the Home's single full-range driver — and all at only $100.</p><p>But how does the speaker actually perform? Is this really a worthy upgrade that can match Amazon's Echo? We've been testing the Google Nest Audio for a while now to find out.</p><h2><strong>Design</strong></h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f8d93da9e9fe4001900a046?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Google nest audio 2\" height=\"843\" width=\"1125\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Christian de Looper/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The <a href=\"https://shop-links.co/1721072491310276872\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Nest Audio</a> represents a major design shift from the older Google Home smart speaker. It fits in style with the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/google-nest-mini-review\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Google Nest Mini</a>, with an all fabric exterior, and a relatively friendly appearance that should look good in most environments. Even better is the fact that it's available in five colors – including Chalk, Charcoal, Sage, Sand, and Sky. We're reviewing the Sage model, but safe to say, there should be something for everyone. And, no matter which color you go for, they're all pretty subtle.&#160;</p><p>The speaker measures a little less than seven inches tall and a little less than five inches wide, and as a result, it's small enough to sit on a table, nightstand, or shelf, without drawing too much attention to itself. It's not battery powered — so you will need to place it relatively close to a power outlet.&#160;</p><p>According to Google, the enclosure of the speaker is made from 70% recycled plastic, which is a nice touch. Tech companies in general are starting to take their environmental impact more seriously, and while they have a <em>long</em> way to go, making their devices from recycled materials is one step in the right direction.</p><p>Google has also been taking privacy a little more seriously, and that shows with the <a href=\"https://shop-links.co/1721072491310276872\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Nest Audio</a>. There's now a physical microphone mute switch on the back of the speaker — so if you don't want to feel like it's always listening, you can move that switch to the off position.</p><p>Capacitive touch controls are found on the top, though you wouldn't know that just by looking at the speaker. You can tap the two top corners to control volume, while the top middle of the device is where you can play or pause your music. On the front of the speaker, there are four LED lights that activate when the Assistant is in use.&#160;</p><p>Generally speaking, the <a href=\"https://shop-links.co/1721072491310276872\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Nest Audio</a> is an attractive speaker, and I appreciate the move towards a simpler, friendlier design compared to the previous model.&#160;</p><h2>Specs</h2><ul><li><strong>Dimensions: </strong>6.89 x 4.89 x 3.07 inches</li><li><strong>Colors: </strong>Chalk, Charcoal, Sage, Sand, Sky</li><li><strong>Connectivity: </strong>802.11/b/g/n/ac Wi-Fi, Bluetooth 5.0</li><li><strong>Speakers: </strong>75mm woofer, 19mm tweeter</li><li><strong>Microphones:</strong> Three far-field microphones</li><li><strong>Smart Assistant: </strong>Google Assistant</li><li><strong>Controls: </strong>Capacitive touch sensors</li><li><strong>Processor: </strong>Quad core A53 1.8GHz</li></ul><h2>Setup and Assistant performance</h2><p>Getting the <a href=\"https://shop-links.co/1721072491310276872\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Nest Audio</a> up and running is incredibly easy with the Google Home app. Once you plug the speaker in and open the Home app, you'll be guided through the setup process. The exact process will vary a little depending on whether or not you've got other Google Assistant devices but, at most, you'll have to sign into your account, record a few sentences for the voice match system, and so on.&#160;</p><p>The setup process also involves linking the speaker to your music streaming service of choice. Currently, you're limited to YouTube Music, Google Play Music, Spotify, Deezer, and Pandora. To be fair, that should encompass the vast majority of Google Assistant fans anyway, since few Google users also have Apple Music, but it would at least be nice to be able to link Amazon Music to your account without having to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/can-google-home-play-amazon-music\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">rely on casting</a>.&#160;</p><p>Google Assistant on the <a href=\"https://shop-links.co/1721072491310276872\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Nest Audio</a> is just as powerful as it always has been. You can use the speaker to control smart home devices, find out information from the web and, as mentioned, play and control music. New for this model, however, is a machine learning chip that Google says will make for faster Assistant responses and some local processing.</p><p>In practice, Google Assistant on the Nest Audio is very responsive, with similar performance as the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/google-nest-mini-review\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Nest Mini</a>. This reliable speed particularly comes into play with voice commands for things like playing and pausing music, changing volume, and so on.&#160;</p><h2>Audio quality</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f8d940ac21cfb0019468b3e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Google nest audio 3\" height=\"843\" width=\"1125\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The Google Nest Audio (left) pictured with the Google Nest Mini (right).\n<p class=\"copyright\">Christian de Looper/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Google is leaning heavily into audio quality for the <a href=\"https://shop-links.co/1721072491310276872\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Nest Audio</a> and, for the most part, the device offers a full-bodied experience that the majority of buyers will love. This is partly thanks to the fact that the speaker has a separate woofer, for low frequencies, and tweeter, for high frequencies, meaning that it can better represent a full range of sound.</p><p>In other words, bass is relatively heavy and strong, though the fact that this is such a small and compact speaker does limit just how deep the low-end can go. Still, most will appreciate the punchy kick drums and smooth bass tones.&#160;</p><p>The speaker especially excels at offering a good amount of clarity and detail for a model in this price range. This means that you'll be able to clearly hear cymbals and percussion, and that there's a good amount of separation between instruments in music. The speaker can get pretty loud for a device its size, and there's little distortion to speak of, which is always good to hear.&#160;</p><p>The \"smart\" part of this smart speaker doesn't just relate to its Google Assistant functions. It also has to do with how the speaker processes audio. The tip of the iceberg is the fact that you can pair two Nest Audio speakers for stereo playback. We only have one for testing, however, so we haven't been able to try this option out ourselves.&#160;</p><p>But, the speaker goes a lot further than that. According to Google, the <a href=\"https://shop-links.co/1721072491310276872\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Nest Audio</a> was tested in thousands of different situations to better tune the speaker for playback in varied environments and placements. This work is all done under the hood, but safe to say the speaker does offer a relatively natural audio response, even in a corner, where bass would traditionally be amplified.&#160;</p><p>Other smart features include Google's Ambient EQ feature, which allows the device to automatically adjust its volume depending on its environment, and a new Media EQ feature, which allows it to automatically tune itself depending on the style of music that you're listening to. As a result, this is one of the smarter smart speakers on the market, whether or not you actually want or will use features like this.&#160;</p><h2>Problems with the Nest Audio</h2><p>The <a href=\"https://shop-links.co/1721072491310276872\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Nest Audio</a> offers incredible value for its price, coming in at only $100 — and that's before any deals or specials that are likely to come up. But it's not <em>perfect</em>.&#160;</p><p>As mentioned, the compact size is nice, but the result is that it can't <em>quite</em> get as deep as we would like. Still, most will be perfectly fine with the bass performance it offers.</p><p>The only other issues, at least when comparing this speaker to the competition from Amazon, are that it doesn't have a 3.5mm port for connecting to an external speaker, or any smart home hub features, like Zigbee connectivity. That latter omission means that you're a bit more limited in the smart home devices that you can connect to your Google account. We would have liked to see Google adopt these features since they will be integrated in the new fourth-generation Echo.</p><h2>The bottom line</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f74d67d0ab50d00184ad622?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Google Nest Audio\" height=\"500\" width=\"1000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Google</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Despite the fact that the <a href=\"https://shop-links.co/1721072491310276872\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Nest Audio</a> doesn't have the same connected home features on offer as other smart speakers, the device is a hit. That's especially true given its price range. At $100, you'd be hard-pressed to find a more well-rounded Google Assistant smart speaker. If you're looking for a new speaker in Google's ecosystem, this is the one to get.</p><h3>What are your alternatives?</h3><p>The <a href=\"https://shop-links.co/1721072491310276872\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Nest Audio</a> does face some stiff competition. Amazon's upcoming fourth-generation Echo could be an especially tempting alternative. The new <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B07XKF5RM3/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&camp=1789&creative=9325&creativeASIN=B07XKF5RM3&linkCode=as2&tag=biip_101620_nest-audio-review-20&linkId=88276691eb3c1a97cc4b0e37affd7d50eb3c1a97cc4b0e37affd7d50\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Echo</a> is also $100 and will come with Zigbee connectivity and a 3.5mm port. We'll have to wait and see how it performs but, ultimately, most buyers will end up picking whichever model fits the smart home ecosystem they're already in.&#160;</p><p>There's also the <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B07NJQFL4X/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&camp=1789&creative=9325&creativeASIN=B07NJQFL4X&linkCode=as2&tag=biip_101620_nest-audio-review-20&linkId=ba4995ddc3b04a009cab934e4bfdd846c3b04a009cab934e4bfdd846\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Sonos One</a> to consider, which is pretty different from the <a href=\"https://shop-links.co/1721072491310276872\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Nest Audio</a>. Despite the Nest Audio's excellent audio chops, the Sonos One still sounds more natural and has better bass response. That said, the Nest Audio offers more smart features, and Google Assistant responds to prompts quite a bit faster on the Nest Audio compared to the Sonos One. You'll have to decide what's more important to you, though given the Sonos One is twice the price of the Nest Audio, most people should save their cash.&#160;&#160;</p><p>If you want a smart speaker that's a solid, all-around speaker for listening to music and controlling Google alike, the <a href=\"https://shop-links.co/1721072491310276872\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Nest Audio</a> is absolutely the way to go.</p><p><strong>Pros: </strong>Friendly design, good audio quality, fast Google Assistant performance, reliable smart features</p><p><strong>Cons: </strong>Bass response could be a little deeper, no smart home hub integration, doesn't include a USB-C port or 3.5 mm jack</p><div border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/eY9UgI3uOyE\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 19 Oct 2020 15:13:55 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5f8d9360c21cfb0019468b3b?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"cf924d6948a0882768893a2a48fb5914","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn64@2020_5/2020/10/19/15-59-22-637_b317d93036a42563.webp","destWidth":1125,"destHeight":843,"sourceBytes":87638,"destBytes":87638,"author":"insider@insider.com (Christian de Looper)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f8d9360c21cfb0019468b3b?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn64@2020_5/2020/10/19/15-59-22-637_b317d93036a42563.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f8d93da9e9fe4001900a046?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn4@2020_3/2020/10/19/15-59-49-405_2c1f3ac0697bcf79.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f8d940ac21cfb0019468b3e?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn16@2020_6/2020/10/19/15-59-47-949_e0e9c63900fa0c95.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f74d67d0ab50d00184ad622?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn55@2020_3/2020/10/19/15-59-46-674_d94ba60c794600cd.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn56@2020_5/2020/10/19/15-59-47-418_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=eY9UgI3uOyE:cE-_9IbM55c:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn28@2020_6/2020/10/19/15-59-41-140_0e1ee3aadde85114.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=eY9UgI3uOyE:cE-_9IbM55c:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn47@2020_1/2020/10/19/15-59-46-563_3c2a5234919908b1.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn91@2020_5/2020/10/19/15-59-43-999_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=eY9UgI3uOyE:cE-_9IbM55c:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn63@2020_6/2020/10/19/15-59-41-534_574aee6498df82f0.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/eY9UgI3uOyE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn32@2020_2/2020/10/19/15-59-41-176_fcd63f0ddf86c0c6.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1603123145993},{"createdTime":"2020-10-19 23:59:06","updatedTime":"2020-10-19 23:59:06","title":"The pandemic has changed how the wealthy buy planes amid a boom of first-time buyers. Here's how sales firms are closing deals amid a global crisis.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-aircraft-sales-firms-are-closing-deals-amid-pandemic-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5a7b247ed0ee001e25e9e9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Dassault Falcon 7X\" height=\"1666\" width=\"2223\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A Dassault Falcon 7X private jet aircraft.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mike Fuchslocher / Shutterstock.com</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Aircraft values have depreciated since the pandemic began in March resulting in a buyer's market but the sales process has been made increasingly difficult due to travel restrictions.&#160;</li>\n<li>Firms are investing resources by bringing planes to buyers instead of having buyers come to the aircraft.&#160;</li>\n<li>When it comes time to close, sellers have to navigate travel restrictions and, in some cases, work with authorities to obtain special permissions when delivering aircraft.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The coronavirus pandemic has emptied the airline terminals only to fill the private terminals as the wealthy shift their travel habits around health and safety. Private aircraft operators are rejoicing as it means more flights for their fleets but an even smaller segment of wealthy flyers are viewing the pandemic as a reason to make the jump into aircraft ownership.</p><p>Acquiring an aircraft comes with unique perks such as unrestricted aircraft availability but comes at a substantially higher cost. Industry veterans say buying an aircraft shouldn't be considered unless a person is spending $500,000 or more on private charter each year.&#160;</p><p>Purchasing an aircraft, unlike buying a car, is an intimate process not only because of the financial commitment but largely due to the fact that an aircraft often serves as a home away from home. Textron Aviation's Senior Vice President of Sales and Flight Operations, Rob Scholl, told Business Insider that his salespeople will travel to prospective buyers and get a sense of their flying needs before recommending an aircraft.&#160;</p><p>Manufacturers like Textron Aviation and aircraft sales firms are once again seeing normal transaction levels but the pandemic has changed the buying process. The cancellation of air shows and industry networking events is making it difficult for firms to get their aircraft in front of potential buyers and travel restrictions are delaying the process when it comes time to close.</p><p>Here's how they're navigating the pandemic to close deals.</p><h2>The right time to buy</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5a9cf5e6ff30001d4e834d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Gulfstream G650ER\" height=\"1334\" width=\"1778\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A Gulfstream G650ER private jet aircraft.\n<p class=\"copyright\">REUTERS/Aly Song</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The immediate aftermath of the pandemic saw aircraft values drop as global travel restrictions largely hindered where people could fly. In some countries, citizens couldn't travel between states, let alone to the other side of the world on a vacation.</p><p>It's created a buyer's market for potential aircraft owners and encouraging the wealthy to purchase aircraft in preparation for when the borders do open.&#160;</p><p>\"There has been some price depreciation since COVID,\" Chad Anderson, president of aircraft sales and acquisition firm Jetcraft, told Business Insider. \"And depending on the model of aircraft, you're looking at probably 10% to 15%, maybe 20% on an older product.\"&#160;</p><p>As the pandemic enters its sixth month and travel restrictions begin to ease, prices are likely the lowest they'll get with Anderson saying the demand is catching up to the supply. Not only is Jetcraft seeing greater than normal number of transactions for this time of year – a typically slow season for aircraft sales – but charter operators are seeing an uptick in their business, indicating a desire to travel.</p><p>\"The best signal we have is that charter market,\" Anderson said. \"When charter market starts to return to business, that's a very healthy, starting point for us\"</p><p>International travel restrictions have not stopped sales for ultra-long-haul aircraft as the pandemic has incurred&#160;pent up demand for cross-border travel. Customers want to be able to jet off to distant locales now more than ever and are making their purchases now so that they don't have to wait even longer for the right aircraft once restrictions do lift.&#160;</p><p>Long-range aircraft from Gulfstream, Dassault, Bombardier are still as popular as ever since they can fly further without stopping compared to smaller jets.&#160;</p><h2>Bringing the plane to the buyer</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5a9cafe6ff30001d4e8349?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Dassault Falcon 7X\" height=\"1665\" width=\"2221\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A Dassault Falcon 7X private jet aircraft.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Fasttailwind / Shutterstock.com</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Pre-pandemic buyers often journey to the aircraft they're seeking to purchase. Though it may seem counterintuitive since the latter is built to travel, flying an aircraft to a customer can negatively impact its value since it incurs more hours on the aircraft, similar to adding miles on a car.</p><p>But travel restrictions have forced sales firms to adapt and bring the product directly to the passengers, at a costly rate. \"We're spending a lot of time and money with airplanes on the road right now,\" said Anderson.</p><p>With even a half-hour flight costing thousands of dollars, firms have to be strategic with to whom they bring the plane for a showing. And much like charter operators, Jetcraft is investing in disinfectants like MicroShield 360 so potential buyers feel comfortable when touring an aircraft.&#160;</p><p>Textron Aviation uses demonstrations flights as a selling point for its buyers, including owners who are also pilots, and has had to revise its procedure for each flight to ensure a safe experience. Personal protective equipment is available to passengers and aircraft are sanitized before and after every flight, Scholl said.&#160;&#160;</p><p>Salespeople are also changing their pitches by familiarizing themselves with the safety features of an aircraft rather than just the onboard luxuries or cost benefits for some owners that come with flying private.&#160;</p><p>\"It was very interesting about how quickly my sales team learned about how quickly the air circulates, how often it's refreshed, and where specifically it goes through the airplane,\" Scholl said, noting that it takes two minutes for the air to recycle on all of Textron's aircraft.&#160;</p><h2>Navigating lockdowns when it's time to buy</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5a9c9ee6ff30001d4e8347?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Cessna Citation CJ3\" height=\"1666\" width=\"2222\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A Textron Aviation Cessna Citation CJ3 private jet aircraft.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mike Fuchslocher / Shutterstock.com</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Both Jetcraft and Textron Aviation have multiple international offices so navigating travel restrictions isn't difficult for salespeople and flight crews, the latter of which are normally exempt from most restrictions, but closing the deal can often be a more time-intensive process.&#160;</p><p>A recent Jetcraft transaction in Europe required the company to convince authorities to open airports that had been closed, waive quarantine restrictions for flight crews, and circumvent international travel restrictions to access a plane at Geneva Airport.</p><p>\"You just have to find a way,\" Pascal Bachmann, Jetcraft's senior vice president of sales in Europe, the Middle East, and Asia, told Business Insider.</p><p>It's often not impossible to close the deals but clearing each new obstacle that the pandemic has put in the way of international commerce often takes longer for deals to be completed. And it's not for lack of cooperation as authorities are often willing to help, according to Bachmann.</p><p>\"I like to say that for the impossible, we need 24 hours delay,\" Bachmann said. \"For miracles, we might need a bit longer.\"</p><p>But the new style of doing business virtually likely won't last in this sector, according to Scholl, as his experience during the pandemic hasn't been too different from normal.</p><p>\"Customers are still coming in here to Wichita to meet with us and go on factory tours,\" Scholl said. \"And I have been out to meet with customers in their homes so I think people still seem to be comfortable with those one-on-one interactions.\"</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a
